(Footnote: 'The complete common notion' is an adjective added to the described, i.e., the complete common thing, which is that for which there is no more specific common notion that applies to the individuals. The difference between it and the true species, despite sharing this meaning, is that the species is the entire quiddity of the individuals and is not a part of it, unlike the genus. And what is said that the species is a part of the individuals and individuation is another part will be refuted by the commentator later as being an accidental not considered. End. al-Shurunbulālī.)
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage, opening a chapter on the principles of concepts (mabādi’ al-taṣawwurāt), expands on the definition of distant genus using the example of growing body (jism nāmī). It explains that growing body is a distant genus for human when compared with horse, but a proximal genus for human when compared with tree. The reason: when asked 'What is human and tree?', 'growing body' is the answer because it covers both (they share only that). But when asked 'What is human and horse?', 'growing body' is insufficient because horse and human share more: animality, which includes sensation and voluntary movement. The complete common notion (tamām al-mushtarak) between human and horse is 'animal' (or 'sentient growing body moving by will'), not just 'growing body'. Al-Dasūqī's commentary reinforces this: the answer for multiple items must be the most specific common attribute. Al-‘Aṭṭār adds that for a plant, growing body is its proximal genus. The footnote by al-Shurunbulālī clarifies 'complete common notion' as the highest common attribute that cannot be further narrowed, and distinguishes it from species: species is the entire quiddity, while genus is a part. The lesson guards against assuming that any shared attribute qualifies as a proximal genus; it must be the 'complete' common notion covering all participants.

Selecting the Correct Genus for Multiple Definitions
Author explains the condition for using a remote genus in multiple questions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of complete commonality to select the correct genus when answering about multiple things.

Core Idea
A remote genus only answers a multiple question if it captures the complete commonality among all items.

When we ask 'What is X and Y?' in Islamic logic, the answer must use a genus that captures everything they have in common. This passage from the Tadhheeb explains that a remote genus only works if it is the complete commonality (tamām al-mushtarak). Let's see how this rule applies to examples from the natural world and why a shared but insufficient genus leads to an incorrect answer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the set of things being asked about
Look at the question: it asks about multiple distinct species. For example, 'What is man and tree?' or 'What is man and horse?'.
2
Determine the remote genus they share
Find a broad genus that both species belong to. For man and tree, that is 'growing body' (al-jism al-nāmī). For man and horse, they share 'growing body' as well.
3
Check if the remote genus is the complete commonality
Ask whether the remote genus includes all shared attributes. If the species share further specific attributes (like animality), then the remote genus is not the complete commonality.
Man and horse also share 'animality' (having sensation and voluntary motion), so 'growing body' alone is insufficient.
4
Select the correct genus for the answer
If the remote genus is not the complete commonality, you must use a more specific genus that captures the full commonality. For man and horse, the correct genus is 'animal' (or 'growing, sensitive, voluntarily moving body').
For man and tree, 'growing body' is the complete commonality, so it is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات
يُشارِكُها هو الجواب عنها وعن الكلِّ ؛ فَبَعِيدٌ، كَالجِسْمِ النَّامِي)، فإنَّه يقع جواباً عن الإنسان وعمَّا يشارِكُه في الجسم النامي فقط، لا عمَّا يشاركه في الحيوانية
·
فإذا قيل: ما الإنسانُ والشَّجر؟ يقع الجسم النامي في الجواب . وأما إذا قيل : ما الإنسانُ والفَرَسُ؟ فلم يقع ـ مع كونهما متشاركين في الجسم النامي - ؛ لأنَّ الفرس لم يشارِكِ الإنسان في الجسم النَّامي فقط ، بل يشاركه في الحيوانية التي هي عبارة عن الجسم النامي الحسّاس المتحرّك بالإرادة، فلا يقعُ الجسمُ النَّامي في الجواب .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : كَالْجِسْمِ النَّامِي حاصلُهُ : أَنَّهُ يقعُ جواباً عنِ السُّؤالِ عَنِ الماهيّةِ الإنسانية، وعن بعض ما شاركها فيه، وهو الشَّجر ، فإذا قِيلَ: مَا الإنسانُ والشَّجر؟ قِيلَ : جسم نام، وَلَا يقعُ جواباً عن الماهيّة، وعن كلِّ مَا شاركَهَا فيه . أَلا ترى أنَّ الفرس والحمار شاركَتِ الإنسان في الجسم النامي، ولا يقع جواباً عن السُّؤالِ عنها ؛ لأنَّ الجواب عن المتعدّدِ ؛ إنَّما يكون بتمام المشترك، وتمام المشترك بينَ الإنسان والحمار والفرس ؛ إِنَّما هو حيوان أو جسم نام حساس مُتحرِّك بالإرادة . (قَوْلُهُ : الَّتِي هِيَ عِبَارَةٌ) أي : معبّر عنها بالجسم النامي ... إلخ؛ لأنَّ الحيوانية معنى يعبر عنها بما ذكر، وليس المرادُ أنَّها لفظ يعبر به عمَّا ذكر
العطار
.
(قَوْلُهُ : كَالْجِسْمِ النَّامِي) يقعُ في الجوابِ عَنِ النَّباتِ والإنسانِ إذا سُئِلَ عنهُمَا بِمَا هوَ، وهو بعينِهِ جواب لِلسُّؤال عن النَّباتِ، وعن كُلِّ واحدٍ ؛ واحدٌ مِمَّا يُشاركُهُ فيه، فهو جنس قريبٌ لِلنَّباتِ، وبعيدٌ لِلإنسان إذا سُئِلَ عنه وعن النَّبَاتِ بِمَا هو ، فإِنْ سُئِلَ عنه وعن الفرس ؛ فليس الجواب إلا الحيوان، ولا يصح أن يُجابَ بِالجسم النَّامي، وقد استشكل التَّمثيل بالجسم النَّامي ؛ بأنَّ الكلام في الكُلِّيَّاتِ المفردة، وأجيب بادّعاءِ أَنَّهُ جعل علماً على مُسمَّاهُ؛ كَعبدِ اللهِ، وسيأتي لذلك بقيَّةٌ .
والمتحرّك بالإرادة، فلا يقعُ الجسمُ النَّامي في الجواب .
Section: On the principles of concepts. [The remote genus] shares with [the species] in the answer about it and about all [that shares with it]; so it is distant, like the growing body. For it occurs as an answer about man and about what shares with him in the growing body only, not about what shares with him in animality. So if it is said: 'What is man and tree?' the growing body occurs in the answer. But if it is said: 'What is man and horse?' it does not occur – despite their sharing in the growing body – because the horse shares with man not only in the growing body, but shares with him in animality, which is expressed as the growing, sensitive, voluntarily moving body. Therefore the growing body does not occur in the answer. Al-Disuqi: His statement: 'like the growing body' – its summary: it occurs as an answer to the question about the human essence and about some of what shares with it, i.e., the tree. So if it is said: 'What is man and tree?' it is said: 'a growing body.' But it does not occur as an answer to the question about the essence and about everything that shares with it. Do you not see that the horse and donkey share with man in the growing body, yet it does not occur as an answer to the question about them? Because the answer concerning multiple things is only by the complete commonality, and the complete commonality between man, donkey, and horse is only animal or a growing, sensitive, voluntarily moving body. His statement: 'which is an expression' – meaning that it is expressed by the growing body, etc., because animality is a meaning expressed by what was mentioned, and it is not intended that it is a word expressed by what was mentioned. Al-Attar: His statement: 'like the growing body' – it occurs in the answer about plants and man if they are asked about what they are, and it is itself the answer to the question about plants, and about each one of what shares with him in it. So it is a proximate genus for plants, and a remote one for man if he is asked about himself and about plants as to what they are. Then if he is asked about him and about the horse, the answer is only animal, and it is not valid to answer with the growing body. And it was objected to the example of the growing body that the discussion is about simple universals, and it was answered by claiming that it was used as a proper name for its referent, like 'Abd Allah, and the remainder of that will come. And the voluntarily moving one, so the growing body does not occur in the answer.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a definitional explanation of the condition for using a remote genus (jins ba'id) in answering 'what is it?' questions about multiple things. The author begins by stating that a remote genus, like 'growing body' (jism nami), can be used as an answer for a species and for everything that shares that genus with it, but only if the genus captures the complete commonality (tamām al-mushtarak) among all the things being asked about. Two examples illustrate this: when asked about man and tree, 'growing body' suffices because they share only that genus. But when asked about man and horse, 'growing body' does not suffice because they share more than that – they also share animality (which includes sensation and voluntary motion). The correct answer in that case is 'animal' or 'growing, sensitive, voluntarily moving body,' which is the complete commonality. The commentators al-Disuqi and al-Atṭār elaborate: al-Disuqi emphasizes that the answer for multiple things must be by the complete commonality, i.e., the most specific genus that includes all shared attributes. Al-Atṭār adds that if the question concerns man and horse, only 'animal' is correct; the objection that 'growing body' is not a simple universal is answered by treating it as a proper name for the referent. The key principle is that a genus used in answers must reflect the full extent of commonality among the subjects.

Key Terms
تمام المشترك
الجسم النامي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When asked 'What is the human and the horse?' why is 'growing body' (jism nami) not a valid answer?
A) Because the human and horse do not share the growing body at all.
B) Because the human and horse share more than just the growing body, namely animality.
C) Because 'growing body' is a proper name and not a universal.
D) Because the question is about multiple things and the answer must be a single simple universal.

Key Takeaway
The rule of complete commonality dictates that the genus used must capture all shared attributes, not just some.

Definition of Species (al-Naw') and Its Place Among Universals
Author defines species (al-naw') as a universal said of many and discusses its definition and order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the definition of species (al-naw') and why the phrase 'said of many' is not a restrictive condition in its definition.

Core Idea
The species is a universal said of many, yet it applies even to a single individual.

The five universals are foundational to definition in Islamic logic. The second universal, species (al-naw'), is defined as 'said of many,' but the commentators clarify that this does not limit species to only multiple individuals. In this lesson, we unpack the definition and the reasoning behind the order of presentation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the universal being defined
Locate in the passage which universal is being discussed and how it is positioned among the five. Note that it is called 'the second' of the universals.
2
Extract the definition phrase
Find the phrase 'al-maqul 'ala al-kathrah' (said of many) and note how the author presents this as the definition of species.
3
Examine the commentary's clarification
Al-Disuqi states that this phrase is 'not a restriction' (laysa bi-qayd). Look at his example: 'What is Zayd? – Human.' How does this example show that species can be predicated of a single individual?
4
Understand the consequence for definition
If 'said of many' is not restrictive, does the definition still work? The commentators suggest it is a prelude to the concept of 'fundamentally agreeing in reality' or that the original state of universals is to be said of many, while being said of one is exceptional.
5
Analyze the order of presentation
Al-ʿAtṭār explains why species is presented before differentia, even though both are parts of the genus. Identify the two reasons he provides: dependency of differentia's division on species, and the order of generality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[النَّوْعُ]
(والثَّانِي) من الكليَّاتِ : (النَّوْعُ : وَهُوَ المُقُوْلُ عَلَى الكَثرَةِ
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : وَالثَّانِي : النَّوْعُ قدَّمَهُ على الفصل، وإنْ كانَ الفصل مشاركاً للجنس في الجزئية؛ لأنَّ تقسيم الفصل إلى مُقوّم ومُقسم؛ مُتوقِّف على مراتبِ النَّوع، وتشارك النوع والجنس في وقوع كل في جواب ما هو؟؛ ولأنَّ النَّوعَ الإضافيَّ مُتَحدٌ مع الجنس القريب بالذاتِ ؛ وإن اختلفا اعتباراً.
(قَوْلُهُ : وَهُوَ الْمَقُوْلُ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ أي: على أفرادها، وهذا ليس بقيد؛ إذ النَّوعُ يحملُ وَلَوْ على الواحدِ ؛ نحو: ما زيدٌ؟، فيُقالُ : الإنسان.
وحينئذٍ؛ لا ينبغي أن يؤخذ في التّعريف، ولعلَّهُ ذكرَهُ توطئةٌ لِقَولِهِ : (المتَّفِقَة (الحقيقة)، أو يُقالُ: إنَّ الأصل في الكُلّيّ أنْ يُقالَ على الكثرة، والمقولية على الوحدة خلاف الأصل.
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ : النَّوْعُ) إِنَّما قَسَّم الجنس على النوع، وأخَّرَ الفصل عنه؛ معَ أَنَّهما جزآنِ لهُ؛ لأنَّ بيانَ المعنى الثَّاني لِلنَّوع يتوقَّفُ على الجنس، وبيان أحكام الفصلِ مِنَ التقويم والتقسيم؛ يتوقَّفُ على النَّوعِ أيضاً، أو لأنَّ أَعَمِّيَّةِ الجنسِ تَقْتَضَى تَقديمَهُ، وأعمِّيَّةُ النَّوع تقتضي تقديمه كما هو المشهور.
[Species]
And the second of the universals: the species, and it is said of many.
Al-Disuqi: His statement: 'And the second: the species' – he presented it before the differentia, even though the differentia shares with the genus in being a part, because the division of the differentia into constitutive and divisive depends on the levels of the species; and the species and genus share in falling in the answer to 'what is it?'; and because the relative species is identical with the proximate genus in essence, though they differ in consideration.
His statement: 'and it is said of many' – i.e., on its individuals. But this is not a restriction, because the species is predicated even on a single one, e.g., 'What is Zayd?' and it is said: 'Human.' Therefore, it should not be taken in the definition; perhaps he mentioned it as a prelude to his statement: 'the [fundamentally] agreeing (in reality),' or it is said: the original in the universal is that it be said of many, while being said of one is contrary to the original.
Al-Attar: His statement: 'the species' – he divided the genus upon the species and delayed the differentia from it, even though they are both parts of it, because the clarification of the second meaning of the species depends on the genus, and the clarification of the rulings of the differentia, such as constituting and dividing, also depends on the species; or because the greater generality of the genus necessitates its presentation, and the greater generality of the species necessitates its presentation as is well-known.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage defines the second of the five universals: the species (al-naw'). The author begins by stating that the species is 'said of many' (maqul 'ala al-kathrah). The commentators immediately clarify this definition. Al-Disuqi notes that the species is placed before the differentia in this classification, even though both are parts of the genus, because the differentia's division (into constitutive and divisive) depends on the levels of species, and because species and genus share in answering 'what is it?' questions. He also explains that the relative species (al-naw' al-idafi) is identical in essence with the proximate genus, differing only in consideration. Regarding the definition 'said of many,' al-Disuqi points out that this is not a restrictive condition (qayd), because the species can be predicated of a single individual (e.g., 'Zayd is human'). So why is it included? Possibly as a prelude to the later concept of 'fundamentally agreeing in reality,' or because the original state of a universal is to be said of many, and being said of one is exceptional. Al-Atṭār adds an explanation of the order: the genus is presented before the species, and the species before the differentia, because understanding the species depends on the genus, and understanding the differentia's roles (constituting and dividing) depends on the species; also the generality order (genus more general, species less general) justifies this sequence.

Key Terms
النوع
المقول على الكثرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because species is always said of many individuals by definition.
C) Because the phrase 'said of many' is only metaphorical.
D) Because the species is identical with the genus in essence.

Key Takeaway
The species is defined as 'said of many,' but this is not a restrictive condition; it can be predicated of a single individual, and the phrase is included due to the original nature of universals or as a prelude to further discussion.

Distinguishing Species from Genus: The Condition of Agreement in Reality
Defines species as the second universal, distinguishing it from genus and other universals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether a universal is a species or a genus by applying the condition of agreement in reality.

Core Idea
Species demands individuals share one essence; genus binds different essences.

In logic, species (al-naw') is a key universal that captures what a thing essentially is. The passage gives a precise definition: 'said of many things agreeing in reality in answer to 'what is it?''. We must carefully apply each condition to avoid confusing species with genus or other universals. This precision is essential for constructing sound definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
The passage defines species (al-naw'). Recognize that it is the second of the five universals, falling under the category of 'said of many'.
2
Extract the defining conditions
The definition has three components: 'said of many' (common to all universals), 'agreeing in reality' (distinguishes from genus), and 'in answer to what is it?' (distinguishes from other universals like differentia and property).
3
Analyze the objection and reply
The objector claims that genus is also said of many agreeing in reality (e.g., 'animal' said of Zayd, Bakr, and a horse). The reply clarifies that the agreement must be from the perspective of the individuals themselves, not because another species is included in the question.
4
Test the definition's exclusivity
Check that the definition includes all species and excludes all non-species (genus, differentia, property, common accident). The objection tests exclusivity, and the reply shows it is maintained.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النَّوْعُ: وَهُوَ الْمَقُولُ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ الْمُتَّفِقَةِ الْحَقِيقَةِ فِي جَوَابِ: مَا هُوَ؟. فَالْمَقُولُ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ جِنْسٌ كَمَا ذَكَرْنَا، وَبِقَيْدِ «الْمُتَّفِقَةِ الْحَقِيقَةِ» يَخْرُجُ الْجِنْسُ، وَبِقَوْلِهِ: «فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ؟» يَخْرُجُ الْبَوَاقِي مِنَ الْكُلِّيَّاتِ. فَخَرَجَ الْعَرَضُ الْعَامُّ، وَخَرَجَ الْفَصْلُ الْقَرِيبُ كَنَاطِقٍ، وَالْخَاصَّةُ كَالضَّاحِكِ. فَإِنْ قُلْتَ: إِنَّ الْجِنْسَ قَدْ يُقَالُ عَلَى الْأَفْرَادِ الْمُتَّفِقَةِ الْحَقِيقَةِ، كَمَا فِي جَوَابِ مَا زَيْدٌ وَبَكْرٌ وَعَمْرٌو وَالْفَرَسُ؟ فَيَصِحُّ أَنْ يُقَالَ فِي الْجَوَابِ: حَيَوَانٌ، فَتَعْرِيفُ النَّوْعِ غَيْرُ مَانِعٍ. وَالْجَوَابُ: أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِقَوْلِهِ: الْمُتَّفِقَةِ الْحَقِيقَةِ، أَيْ: مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّهَا مُتَّفِقَةٌ، فَقَيْدُ الْحَيْثِيَّةِ مُعْتَبَرٌ فِي التَّعْرِيفِ. فَأَمَّا مَقُولِيَّةُ الْجِنْسِ فِي الْمِثَالِ الْمَذْكُورِ عَلَى زَيْدٍ وَعَمْرٍو وَبَكْرٍ فَلَيْسَ مِنْ حَيْثُ اتِّفَاقُهَا فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ، بَلْ مِنْ حَيْثُ وُجُودُ الْمُشَارَكِ لَهَا فِي السُّؤَالِ الْمُخَالِفِ لَهَا فِي الْحَقِيقَةِ، وَهُوَ الْفَرَسُ.
Species: It is what is said of many things agreeing in reality in answer to 'What is it?'. So what is said of many is genus as we mentioned, and by the condition 'agreeing in reality' genus is excluded, and by his statement 'in answer to what is it?' the remaining universals are excluded. Thus, common accident is excluded, and the proximate differentia like 'rational' and the property like 'laughing' are excluded. If you say: 'Genus is indeed said of individuals agreeing in reality, as in answering what is Zayd, Bakr, Amr and the horse? For one may answer: animal. So the definition of species is not exclusive.' The answer: 'What is meant by his statement "agreeing in reality" is from the perspective of their agreement, so the perspective condition is considered in the definition. As for the predication of genus in the mentioned example on Zayd, Amr, and Bakr, it is not from the perspective of their agreement in reality, but from the perspective of the existence of a participant with them in the question that differs in reality, namely the horse.'
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage defines the second of the five universals: species (al-naw'). The definition given is: 'what is said of many things agreeing in reality in answer to 'what is it?'' The author then explains each condition. The phrase 'said of many' is the same for genus, but genus is said of many differing in reality, so adding 'agreeing in reality' excludes genus. The phrase 'in answer to 'what is it?'' excludes the other universals: common accident (arad 'amm) answers 'what kind?', proximate differentia (fasl qarib) answers 'what? but without agreement in reality?', and property (khassa) answers 'which one?' not 'what is it?'. The commentator anticipates an objection: genus is also said of many individuals agreeing in reality, as when asking about Zayd, Bakr, Amr, and a horse, one can answer 'animal' for all. This would make the definition not exclusive (ghayr mani'). The answer clarifies that the condition 'agreeing in reality' is considered from the perspective of the individuals themselves (their essences) when they are all of the same species. In the objection, the genus 'animal' is said of Zayd, Bakr, and Amr not because they agree in reality (since they are human and the horse is also animal), but because there is a participant (the horse) that differs in reality, forcing a general answer that covers both humans and horses. Thus species is defined as that which is said of many agreeing in reality in themselves, without mixing with another species.

Key Terms
النَّوْعُ (al-naw'): The second of the five universals; what is said of many things that agree in their essence in answer to 'what is it?' [Note: No significant shift—stable across the logical tradition.]
الْمُقُولُ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ (al-maqūl 'alā al-kathrah): Predicated on many individuals; a universal's characteristic of applying to multiple instances. [Note: This phrase is standard for all universals; specific definitions distinguish each universal.]
الْمُتَّفِقَةِ الْحَقِيقَةِ (al-muttafiqah al-ḥaqīqah): Agreeing in reality; the individuals share a single essence or quiddity. [Note: This condition excludes genus, which applies to individuals differing in essence.]
فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ (fī jawāb mā huwa): In answer to 'what is it?'; the categorical question that asks for the essence. [Note: This phrase is standard for species and genus; different questions distinguish other universals.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is excluded by the condition 'agreeing in reality' in the definition of species?
A) Common accident
B) Genus
C) Property
D) Differentia

Key Takeaway
Species is defined as a universal predicated on many individuals that share a single essence when asked about their quiddity, excluding genus and other universals through precise conditions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the definition of 'zakat' as 'a specific charity on specific wealth for specific recipients', identify which parts correspond to the genus ('charity') and the differentia ('specific wealth, specific recipients') according to the species definition template.
?
Construct a definition for 'riba' (usury) using the species template: ensure it includes agreement in reality (all riba transactions share an essence) and answers 'what is it?' (it is interest on loans), excluding other forms of trade.

Species as Complete Quiddity and the Objection from Accidents
Author defines species and answers an objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define species as the complete quiddity of individuals and refute the objection that individuating accidents prevent species from being the complete essence.

Core Idea
Species is the complete quiddity; predication on one individual is accidental.

This lesson unpacks the foundational definition of species (al-naw') in Islamic logic. The author asserts that species is the complete quiddity (tamam al-mahiyya) shared by all individuals, making them identical in essence. However, an objection arises: each individual also possesses unique accidents (tashakhkhus), so how can the species alone be the complete quiddity? The commentary resolves this by distinguishing between essential and accidental predication, grounding the definition firmly in the answer to 'what is it?'.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of species
Find the sentence where the author defines species as the complete quiddity of individuals. Note that this is the core claim being established.
The definition appears at the beginning of the passage: 'Since the species is the complete quiddity of individuals'.
2
Identify the function of species in answering 'what is it?'
The passage shows that the same species name (e.g., 'human') serves as the correct answer when asking about one individual or a group. This proves that the species captures the complete essence across individuals.
Example: 'What is Zayd?' → 'Human'; 'What are Zayd, Amr, and Bakr?' → 'Human'.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection claims that each individual includes both the species (e.g., human) and individuating accidents (e.g., whiteness, tallness). Therefore, the species cannot be the complete quiddity; it is merely a part. Understand the logical basis of this challenge.
The objection is presented as: 'Each individual includes the species and individuation, so the species is not the complete quiddity, but a part.'
4
Examine the commentator's response
Al-Dasuqi explains that the species being said of one individual is accidental (arid), due to the individuals sharing the same reality. The primary principle (asl) is that a universal is predicated of many. The author's phrase 'upon multiplicity' refers to this principle.
The response emphasizes that accidental predication does not undermine the essential completeness of the species.

فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات وَلَمَّا كَانَ النَّوعُ تَمَامَ مَاهِيَّةِ الْأَفْرَادِ ; تَكُونُ أَفْرَادُهُ مُتَّفِقَةَ الْحَقِيقَةِ، فَإِذَا سُئِلَ عَنْ أَحَدِهَا أَوْ عَنْ جَمِيعِهَا ; صَلَحَ النَّوعُ فِي الْجَوَابِ، كَمَا إِذَا قِيلَ : مَا زَيْدٌ ؟ كَانَ الْجَوَابُ : الْإِنْسَانُ، وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا قِيلَ : مَا زَيْدٌ وَعَمْرُو وَبَكْرٌ؟ . فَإِنْ قِيلَ : كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ أَفْرَادِ النَّوعِ مُشْتَمِلٌ عَلَى النَّوعِ وَعَلَى التَّشَخُّصِ، فَلَا يَكُونُ النَّوعُ تَمَامَ مَاهِيَّةِ الْأَفْرَادِ، بَلْ يَكُونُ جُزْءاً لَهَا .الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ: وَلَمَّا كَانَ النَّوْعُ ... إلخ) جواب عمَّا يُقالُ: إِنَّ النَّوعَ كَمَا يُقالُ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ; يُقالُ عَلَى الْوَاحِدِ . وَحَاصِلُ الْجَوَابِ أَنَّ مَقوليَّتَهُ عَلَى الْوَاحِدِ أَمْرٌ عَارِضٌ; مِن كَوْنِ أَفْرَادِهِ مُتَّفِقةً الْحَقِيقَةَ . وَالْأَصْلُ فِي الْكُلّيِّ أَنْ لَا يُقَالَ إِلَّا عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ، فَقَوْلُ الْمُصَنِّفِ : عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ نَاظِرٌ لِلْأَصْلِ . (قَوْلُهُ : تَمَامَ مَاهِيَّةِ الْأَفْرَادِ ) أي : الْمَاهِيَّةُ التَّامَّةُ لِلأَفْرَادِ. (قَوْلُهُ: فَإِذَا سُئِلَ ... إلخ) هُوَ وَجَوَابُهُ ; جَوَابُ «لَمَّا»، فَالْأَوْلَى حَذْفُ الْفَاءِ; لِأَنَّ جَوَابَ لَمَّا»; لَا يَقْتَرِنُ بِالْفَاءِ إِلَّا عَلَى طَرِيقَةٍ مَرْجُوحَةٍ، أَوْ أَنَّ جَوَابَ لَمَّا» مَحْذُوفٌ ; دَلَّ عَلَيْهِ جَوَابُ «إِذَا»; أَيْ : صَلَحَ لِأَنْ يُقَالَ فِي الْجَوَابِ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ وَالْوَاحِدِ . وَقَوْلُهُ : فَإِذَا سَأَلَ مُسْتَأْنَفٌ : هَذَا كُلُّهُ عَلَى نُسْخَةٍ: لِكَوْنِ أَفْرَادِ بِاللَّامِ، وَفِي نُسْخَةٍ : بِكَوْنِ بِالْبَاءِ، وَعَلَيْهَا ; فَالْبَاءُ مُتَعَلِّقَةٌ بِمَحْذُوفٍ جَوَابِ لَمَّا ; أَيْ : جَزَمْنَا بِكَوْنِ . . . إلخ . (قَوْلُهُ : صَلَحَ النَّوْعُ ... إلخ) جَوَابُ لَمَّا، وَجَوَابُ «إِذَا» مَحْذُوفٌ مُمَاثِلٌ لَهُ، أَوْ بِالْعَكْسِ، وَالْأَوَّلُ أَقْيَسُ. (قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنْ قِيلَ : ... إِلَخ) هَذَا وَارِدٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ : (وَلَمَّا كَانَ . . . إلخ). (قَوْلُهُ : وَعَلَى التَّشَخُّصِ) أَيْ : كَـ: (الْبَيَاضِ، وَالسَّوَادِ، وَالْقَصَرِ).العطار الْكَثْرَةِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ فِي جَوَابِ مَا هُوَ ؟ ; الْمَقُولُ عَلَيْهَا صَرِيحاً; لَا ضِمْناً ا.هـ. أَوْ أَنَّ : قَيْدَ فَقَطْ مَلْحُوظٌ مُرَادٌ، أَوِ التَّقْيِيدُ بِالْحَيْثِيَّةِ مُعْتَبَرٌ .
Chapter on the principles of concepts. Since the species is the complete quiddity of individuals, its individuals are identical in reality. So if asked about one of them or about all of them, the species is suitable as an answer, as when it is said: 'What is Zayd?' the answer is 'human', and likewise if it is said: 'What are Zayd, Amr, and Bakr?' If it is said: 'Each individual of the species includes the species and individuation (tashakhkhus), so the species is not the complete quiddity of individuals, but rather a part of them.' [al-Dasuqi:] His statement: 'Since the species... etc.' is an answer to what is said: 'The species, just as it is said of multiplicity, is said of the one.' The summary of the answer is that its being said of the one is an accidental matter, due to its individuals being identical in reality. The principle regarding the universal is that it is only said of multiplicity, so the author's statement 'upon multiplicity' refers to the principle. His statement: 'complete quiddity of individuals' means the complete quiddity for individuals. His statement: 'So if asked... etc.' [Discussion of grammar: the response of 'lamma' etc.] His statement: 'So if it is said... etc.' This is an objection to his statement: 'Since the species... etc.' His statement: 'and upon individuation' i.e. like whiteness, blackness, shortness. [al-Attar:] ...the multiplicity of different [things] in answer to 'what is it?' that which is said explicitly, not implicitly. Or that the restriction 'only' is intended and observed, or the restriction by aspect is considered.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage defines the species (al-naw') and clarifies its role in answering 'what is it?' (ma huwa). The author begins by stating that since the species is the complete quiddity (tamam al-mahiyya) of its individuals, all individuals of that species share the same reality. This means that whether you ask about a single individual or a group of them, the species name is the correct answer. For example, when asked 'What is Zayd?' the answer is 'human,' and when asked 'What are Zayd, Amr, and Bakr?' the answer is also 'human.' The passage then presents an objection: each individual includes not only the species but also individuating accidents (such as whiteness, blackness, or shortness). Therefore, the species cannot be the complete quiddity; it can only be a part. The commentary by al-Dasuqi responds that the species is indeed said of the one individual, but this is an accidental (arid) predication due to the fact that all individuals share the same reality. The primary principle (asl) is that a universal is predicated of multiplicity. Therefore, when the author says 'upon multiplicity,' he is referring to the principle. Al-Dasuqi explains the grammatical structure: the 'lamma' clause is answered by the 'idha' clause or vice versa. Al-Attar adds that the restriction ('only') is either explicit or implicit. Overall, the passage establishes that species is the complete essence in answer to 'what is it?' and addresses the potential confusion that arises from individuals having additional accidents.

Key Terms
النوع (al-naw'): The universal that is predicated of many individuals differing in number, and in this passage it is defined as the complete quiddity (tamam al-mahiyya) of its individuals. [Note: In earlier logic, naw' is often defined as a universal predicated of many in answer to 'what is it?' without specifying 'complete quiddity'; this text emphasizes completeness.]
تمام الماهية (tamam al-mahiyya): The complete essence of a thing, which includes all essential parts; for species, it is the entire quiddity shared by all individuals. [Note: No significant shift.]
التشخص (al-tashakhkhus): Individuation or the set of accidental properties that distinguish one individual from another within a species. [Note: In philosophy, tashakhkhus may refer to the principle of individuation; here it is simply the collection of accidents.]
مقولية على الكثرة (maquliyya 'ala al-kathra): Predication of a universal upon many individuals; the fundamental characteristic of universals. [Note: Stable across the tradition.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it correct to answer 'human' for both 'What is Zayd?' and 'What are Zayd, Amr, and Bakr?'
A) Because species is the complete quiddity shared by all individuals.
B) Because human is the genus of Zayd.
C) Because individuals have no accidents.
D) Because species is predicated only on multiplicity.

Key Takeaway
Species is the complete quiddity of its individuals, and its predication on a single individual is accidental, not essential.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'zakat' as 'a specified portion of wealth given to specific categories of recipients'. The Species as Complete Essence of Individuals
Author defines the species as the complete essence of individuals and defends against the objection that individuation makes it merely a part.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the species is the complete essence of individuals and distinguish between essential quiddity and accidental individuation.

Core Idea
The species fully answers 'what is it?' because individuating traits are accidental, not essential.

In this passage from a logic textbook, the author establishes that the species (al-nawʿ) constitutes the complete quiddity of its individuals. He defends this against the objection that individuals also include unique features (tashakhkhuṣ). Understanding this distinction is crucial for mastering the five universals and for constructing precise definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and the claim
Find the term being defined (النوع) and the author's claim: it is the complete essence (تمام الماهية) of individuals. This means when asked 'What is it?' about any individual, the species alone suffices as the answer.
The claim is that individuals are identical in reality (الحقيقة) at the species level.
2
Examine the supporting example
Consider the example: 'What is Zayd?' Answer: 'Human.' The same answer works for all individuals (Zayd, Amr, Bakr). This shows the species captures their shared essence.
The example illustrates that the species is predicable of many differing in number.
3
Understand the objection
The objector argues each individual contains both the species and individuation (التشخيص), so the species is only a part, not the whole essence.
This is a common challenge: how can a universal fully describe a particular?
4
Analyze the response
The author replies that individuation is accidental (عارض) and not considered part of the quiddity (ماهية). Therefore, what is essential is entirely captured by the species.
The key move is distinguishing between essential and accidental attributes.
5
Extract the logical principle
Conclude that a universal like 'human' expresses the complete 'what' of individuals; accidents like height or location do not affect the quiddity. This principle underpins the use of species in definitions across Islamic sciences.
This is foundational for hadd and rasm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات وَلَمَّا كَانَ النَّوْعُ تَمَامَ مَاهِيَّةِ الْأَفْرَادِ ؛ تَكُونُ أَفْرَادُهُ مُتَّفِقَةَ الْحَقِيقَةِ، فَإِذَا سُئِلَ عَنْ أَحَدِهَا أَوْ عَنْ جَمِيعِهَا ؛ صَلَحَ النَّوْعُ فِي الْجَوَابِ، كَمَا إِذَا قِيلَ : مَا زَيْدٌ ؟ كَانَ الْجَوَابُ : الْإِنْسَانُ، وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا قِيلَ : مَا زَيْدٌ وَعَمْرٌو وَبَكْرٌ؟ . فَإِنْ قِيلَ : كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ أَفْرَادِ النَّوْعِ مُشْتَمِلٌ عَلَى النَّوْعِ وَعَلَى التَّشْخُصِ، فَلَا يَكُونُ النَّوْعُ تَمَامَ مَاهِيَّةِ الْأَفْرَادِ، بَلْ يَكُونُ جُزْءاً لَهَا . قُلْتُ : التَّشْخِيصُ عَارِضٌ غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَرٍ فِي مَاهِيَّةِ تِلْكَ الْأَفْرَادِ، فَالنَّوْعُ تَمَامُ الْمَاهِيَّةِ.
Section: On the principles of concepts. When the species is the complete essence of individuals, its individuals are identical in reality. So if one asks about one of them or all of them, the species is correct in the answer, as when it is said: 'What is Zayd?' the answer is 'Human'; and likewise when it is said: 'What are Zayd, Amr, and Bakr?' Then if it is said: 'Each individual of the species includes the species and individuation, so the species is not the complete essence of the individuals, but rather a part of them.' I say: Individuation is accidental, not considered in the quiddity of those individuals, so the species is the complete quiddity.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This is a definitional passage from a textbook on logic, specifically about the species (al-nawʿ) and its relation to individuals. The author begins by stating that the species is the complete essence of individuals, meaning that when asked about an individual's 'whatness' (mā hiyya), the species suffices. For example, Zayd is a human, and that definition covers all humans. An objection is raised: each individual includes both the species and its individuating characteristics (tashakhkhuṣ), so the species cannot be the whole essence; it is only a part. The author responds by distinguishing between essence and accident: individuation is an accidental (ʿāriḍ) feature not considered in the quiddity of individuals. Therefore, the species remains the complete answer. This teaches that universals like 'human' capture the essence, while particular differences are incidental.

Key Terms
النوع
تمام الماهية
التشخيص
عارض

C) Because individuation is accidental and not part of the quiddity.

Key Takeaway
The species provides the complete answer to 'what is it?' because individuating accidents do not affect the quiddity.

Tashkhees: Accident in Essence, Part of the Individual
Commentators refine whether tashkhees is part of the species essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two senses of determination (ta'ayyun) and explain why tashkhees is considered an accident in the species essence yet a part of the individual.

Core Idea
Tashkhees is part of the individual but not part of the species essence.

In this passage, commentators refine the claim that particularization (tashkhees) is an accidental feature not included in the essence of individuals. They reconcile this with the fact that tashkhees clearly defines individual identity. By distinguishing between the individual's conceptual part and the species' essence, they preserve both universality and concrete reality. We will follow their reasoning and analyze an objection concerning the difference between Zayd and Amr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base claim
Find the statement 'al-tashkhees 'arid ghayr mu'tabar fi mahiyyat tilka al-afrad'. What does it assert about tashkhees and the species essence?
The claim is that tashkhees is an accident not considered in the species essence.
2
Unpack al-Dasuqi's reconciliation
How does al-Dasuqi show that being an accident does not prevent tashkhees from being part of the individual? He says it is part of individuals like Zayd and Amr, but not part of the species' mahiyya.
This resolves the apparent contradiction with earlier statements.
3
Distinguish the two senses of ta'ayyun
From al-'Attar and Mir Zahid, identify the two meanings: (1) impossibility of sharing (mental form), (2) distinctness from others (by particular existence).
This clarifies that determination is not a rational or external part of the species.
4
Analyze the conditional objection
The objector argues: if tashkhees is not in the person's reality, then the difference between Zayd and Amr is merely conceptual. How does al-'Attar respond? He distinguishes difference in reality vs. difference in reference (ishara), denying the implication.
This is a conditional argument: If P then Q, but Q is ambiguous.
5
Identify the role of external existence
According to al-'Attar, what is the actual particularizer? External existence (al-wujud al-khariji). Accidents are only indicators.
This is supported by the principle that accidents are individuated by their subjects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلتُ : التَّشخيص عارض غير معتبر في ماهية تلك الأفراد، فالنَّوعُ تمام الماهية.
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : عَارِضٌ ) أي : أمر طارئ على الماهية، وهذا لا يُنافي دخوله في مفهوم الأفراد، وأنَّه جزء منها كـ : زيد، وعَمْرو مثلاً ، فَندفعُ مَا يُقالُ: إِنَّ كَلامَ الشّارِحِ هنا مُخالف لِمَا ذكره سابقاً في الكلام على الحيوانِ النَّاطِقِ علماً؛ من أنَّ التَشَخْصَ جزء مِنَ الأفراد، وذكر هنا أنَّهُ عارض، وغير معتبر في ماهية الأفراد. وحاصل الجوابِ : أَنَّ التَّشخُصَ وإِنْ كانَ غير مُعتبر في ماهية الأفراد؛ إِلَّا أَنَّه جزء منها، ولا ضرر في أنَّهُ جزء من الأفراد، وغير معتبر جزءاً في ماهيتها .
المطار
(قَوْلُهُ : غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَرٍ فِي مَاهِيَّةِ تِلْكَ الأَفْرَادِ وإِنْ كانَ مُعتبراً في مُسمَّاهَا الَّذي هو الشَّخصُ الخارجي؛ وهو الهوية، قال عبد الحكيم : التَشخُصُ عارض للنَّوع، نِسبتُهُ إليه نسبة الفصل إلى الجنس ؛ جزءٌ للشَّخص .ا.هـ. وفي حاشية مير زاهد أنَّ التَّعيُّنَ ليسَ دَاخِلاً في حقيقة الجزئي وليسَ نِسبتُهُ إلى النَّوعِ كَنِسبةِ الفصل إلى الجنس؛ على ما زعمه كثيرٌ مِنَ المتأخّرينَ، فإنّهُ لو كانَ جُزءاً عقليًّا ؛ لَكَانَ محمولاً، ولو كان جزءاً خارجيًا ؛ لَكَانَ النَّوعُ جزءاً خارجيًّا غير محمول، وتحقيق المقام أنَّ التَّعيُّنَ يُطلَقُ على معنيين ؛ الأَوَّل: كونُ الشَّيء بحيثُ يمتنع فرضُ اشتراكه بينَ كَثيرين، وهو يحصل من نحو الوجودِ في الذهن ويلحقُ الصُّوَرَ الذّهنيَّةَ مِن حيثُ إِنَّها صورة ذهنيّةٌ؛ لأنَّ الحمل والانطباق وما يقابلهُمَا مِن شأنِ الصُّوَرِ ؛ دونَ الأعيانِ، والثَّاني : كونُ الشَّيءِ مُمتازاً عَمَّا عداه، وهو يحصلُ بالوجودِ الخاص، بمعنى أنَّ الشَّيءَ يَصيرُ بالوجودِ الخاص ممتازاً عَمَّا عداه، كما أَنَّهُ يَصيرُ بِهِ مصدراً لِلآثَارِ، وقال الفارابي في تعليقاتِهِ : هو الشَّيءُ ، وتَعينُه ، ووحدته، وخصوصيَّته ووجوده المنفرد واحدٌ لا يقالُ : لو لم يكن التَّشخُصُ داخِلاً في حقيقةِ الشَّخص ؛ لكانَ التغايرُ بين زيدٍ وعَمْرِو اعتباريًا، وهو باطل بالضَّرورةِ، لأنَّا نقولُ : إِنْ أُريدَ بالتَّغاير بينَهُما ؛ التَّغاير بحسب الحقيقة؛ فبطلانُ التّالي ممنوع، وإِنْ أُريدَ بِهِ التَّغَايرُ بحسبِ الإشارة ; فَالملازمه ممنوعةٌ، فإنَّ الشَّيء كَمَا يصيرُ بالوجود مصدراً للآثار ; كذلك يصيرُ بِهِ مُمتازاً عَمَّا عداه، ثمَّ إِنَّ الأعراض اللاحقة للأشخاص؛ لَيسَتْ قائمةٌ بِهَا ، بل بموادّها، وإلا ; يلزمُ الدَّورُ ; لأنَّ الأعراضَ مُتشخّصةٌ بِمحالها، والحقُّ أَنَّ الوجود الخارجي هو المشخّصُ، وأمَّا الأعراض ; فَهيَ أمارات له، ويمكنُ أنْ ينبه عليهِ بأنَّ تمايزَ العَرَضَيْن المتماثلين ; يحصلُ مِن وجودِهِمَا في الموضوعين، و تمايز الصُّورتَين المتماثلتين يحصل مِن وجودِهِمَا في المادَّتَيْنِ، وقد تقرَّرَ في مَوضِعِهِ أنَّ وجودَ العَرَضِ ; هو بعينه وجوده في الموضوع , ووجودَ الصُّورة; هو بعينه وجودها في المادَّةِ فَتَفَطَّنْ، فإنَّهُ يحتاج إلى لُطفِ القريحة ا.هـ.
I say: Particularization is an accident not considered in the essence of those individuals, so the species is the complete essence. al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'accident') means something that supervenes upon the essence, and this does not preclude its entry into the concept of individuals, and that it is part of them, like Zayd and Amr for example. So it repels what is said: that the statement of the commentator here contradicts what he mentioned earlier in discussing 'rational animal' as a science, that particularization is part of individuals, and he mentioned here that it is an accident not considered in the essence of individuals. The sum of the answer: that particularization, even if not considered in the essence of individuals, yet it is part of them, and there is no harm in its being part of individuals while not considered as part in their essence. al-'Attar: (His saying: 'Not considered in the essence of those individuals' while it is considered in its referent which is the external person, and it is the identity. 'Abd al-Hakim said: Particularization is an accident of the species, its relation to it is like the relation of differentia to genus; it is a part of the person. End quote. And in the marginalia of Mir Zahid, that determination is not included in the reality of the particular, and its relation to the species is not like the relation of differentia to genus, as many later scholars claim. For if it were a rational part, it would be predicable; and if it were an external part, then the species would be an external part that is not predicated. The investigation of the matter is that determination is used in two senses: first, the thing being such that its sharing among many is impossible, and this occurs from something like existence in the mind and attaches to mental forms insofar as they are mental forms, because predication, applicability, and their opposites are properties of forms, not of external entities. The second: the thing being distinct from others, and this occurs by particular existence, meaning that the thing becomes by particular existence distinct from others, just as it becomes by it a source of effects. And al-Farabi said in his commentary: the thing, its determination, its unity, its particularity, and its singular existence are one. One cannot say: if particularization were not included in the reality of the person, then the difference between Zayd and Amr would be conceptual, and that is evidently false. Because we say: if by 'difference between them' is meant difference in reality, then the falsity of the consequent is not conceded; and if is meant difference in reference, then the implication is not conceded. For just as the thing becomes by existence a source of effects, so it becomes by it distinct from others. Then indeed the accidents attaching to persons are not subsistent in them, but rather in their matters; otherwise, circularity would follow, because accidents are particularized by their loci. The truth is that external existence is the particularizer, and as for accidents, they are indicators of it. One can alert to this by that the differentiation of two similar accidents occurs by their existence in two subjects, and the differentiation of two similar forms occurs by their existence in two matters. And it has been established in its place that the existence of an accident is exactly its existence in the subject, and the existence of a form is exactly its existence in matter. So pay attention, for it requires subtlety of mind. End quote.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the claim that particularization (tashkhees) is an accident not considered in the essence of individuals, while the species constitutes the complete essence. Al-Dasuqi first clarifies that being an accident does not prevent tashkhees from being part of the concept of an individual; it is part of individuals like Zayd and Amr, but not part of their essence as a species. This resolves an apparent contradiction with an earlier statement where tashkhees was called a part of individuals. The core answer is that tashkhees is part of the individual but not part of its quiddity (mahiyya). Al-'Attar then expands, explaining that 'not considered in essence' means it is not a constituent of the species' quiddity, though it is considered in the external person's identity. He quotes 'Abd al-Hakim, who likens tashkhees's relation to the species to that of differentia to genus – it is a part of the person. However, Mir Zahid's marginalia object that determination (ta'ayyun) is not a part of the particular's reality; if it were a rational part it would be predicable, and if an external part it would make the species non-predicable. Al-'Attar resolves this by distinguishing two senses of ta'ayyun: (1) the impossibility of sharing, which attaches to mental forms; (2) distinctness from others, which occurs by particular existence (al-wujud al-khass). He cites al-Farabi for the unity of thing and its determination. Then he addresses an objection: if tashkhees were not inside the person's reality, the difference between Zayd and Amr would be merely conceptual, which is absurd. The answer is that this depends on what is meant by 'difference' – if difference in reality, the consequent is not conceded; if difference in reference (ishara), the implication is denied. Finally, he argues that the true particularizer is external existence, not accidents; accidents are merely indicators. This is supported by the principle that accidents and forms are individuated by their subjects or matter. The passage concludes with a call for subtle understanding.

Key Terms

ماهية
عرض
التعين

A) Their particularization (tashkhees) as an accident
B) Their external existence (al-wujud al-khariji)
C) Their accidental qualities
D) Their matter and form

Key Takeaway
The discussion shows that tashkhees is a part of the individual but not part of the species essence, a distinction that preserves both the universality of definitions and the reality of individuals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the hadith: 'The best of you are those who learn the Qur'an and teach it.' The individual Zayd is not part of the essence of 'the one who learns'. Explain why this does not make the difference between Zayd and Amr merely conceptual, using the distinction between difference in reality and difference in reference.
?
In the definition of 'human' as 'rational animal', is 'rationality' part of the essence or an accident? How does this compare to tashkhees? Explain why tashkhees is not a differentia but an accident of the species.

Defining Relative Species (al-Naw' al-Idafi)
Author defines relative species and distinguishes it from absolute species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that makes a species 'relative' and distinguish it from the real species.

Core Idea
A relative species is a universal essence predicated of itself and of another thing that is its genus.

In Islamic logic, the term 'species' is used in two senses: real and relative. The relative species is defined not by the unity of its individuals alone but by its relation to a higher genus. This lesson dissects the definition given in the matn and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Locate the term being defined: al-naw' al-idafi (النوع الإضافي). The passage clarifies that this is a secondary usage of 'species', indicated by the particle 'qad' (قد) for rarity.
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The definition states: 'the universal essence that is predicated of itself and of other than itself: the genus, in answer to what is it?' Here the genus is 'universal essence' (al-mahiyya al-kulliyya) and the differentia is 'predicated of itself and of another that is its genus'.
This is not a strict hadd but a rasm (descriptive definition).
3
Understand the correlativity
Al-'Attar explains that the relative species is so called because its species-ness depends on being subsumed under a genus alongside another species, creating a mutual relation (mudaafa). Just as father and son are correlatives, the genus and the subsumed species are correlatives.
4
Contrast with real species
The real species (al-naw' al-haqiqi) does not require a higher genus; its species-ness arises from the unity of reality in its individuals. The relative species is defined by the condition that it is predicated of itself and of another (its genus).
This contrast helps avoid confusing the two meanings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات
(وَقَدْ يُقَالُ)؛ أي: كما يقالُ النَّوعُ على المعنى المذكور، كذلك يقال النَّوعُ عَلَى المَاهِيَّةِ الكُلِّيَّةِ المقُوْلِ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا: «الجِنْسُ»، فِي جَوَاب : مَا هُوَ؟
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ: وَقَدْ يُقَالُ) «قد» للتقليل ؛ أي: قد يُطلَقُ، ويحمل لفظ النَّوعِ بقلة . (قَوْلُهُ : الْمَقُوْلِ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا الْجِنْسُ خرج به الجنس العالي، والنَّوع البسيط، والنّوع المركَّب من أمرين متساويين، فكلُّ واحدٍ من هذه الثَّلاثةِ لا يكونُ نوعاً إضافيا ؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُقالُ عليه وعلى غيره جنس .
العطار
يصيرُ بِهِ مُمتازاً عَمَّا عداه، ثمَّ إِنَّ الأعراض اللاحقة للأشخاص؛ لَيسَتْ قائمةٌ بِهَا ، بل بموادّها، وإلا ; يلزمُ الدَّورُ ; لأنَّ الأعراضَ مُتشخّصةٌ بِمحالها، والحقُّ أَنَّ الوجود الخارجي هو المشخّصُ، وأمَّا الأعراض ; فَهيَ أمارات له، ويمكنُ أنْ ينبه عليهِ بأنَّ تمايزَ العَرَضَيْن المتماثلين ; يحصلُ مِن وجودِهِمَا في الموضوعين، و تمايز الصُّورتَين المتماثلتين يحصل مِن وجودِهِمَا في المادَّتَيْنِ، وقد تقرَّرَ في مَوضِعِهِ أنَّ وجودَ العَرَضِ ; هو بعينه وجوده في الموضوع , ووجودَ الصُّورة; هو بعينه وجودها في المادَّةِ فَتَفَطَّنْ، فإنَّهُ يحتاج إلى لُطفِ القريحة ا.هـ. (قَوْلُهُ : وَقَدْ يُقَالُ) أي : يطلقُ ويحملُ، وأشار بكلمة «قد» إلى أنَّ استعمال النَّوع بالمعنى الأوَّلِ أكثرُ ، وإِنَّما سُمِّيَ إضافيًّا ؛ لأَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ فِي نَوْعِيَّتِهِ مِن اندراجِهِ مِن نوع آخَرَ تحتَ جنسٍ، فيكون مُضايفاً له، فالجنس والنَّوعُ المندرج تحته مُتَضايفَانِ كالأب والابن وأمَّا نوعيَّةُ النّوع الحقيقيّ؛ فَهِيَ نِسبةٌ وإضافةٌ بينَهُ وبينَ أفراده، فليس يعتبر فيها إلا حقيقة أفرادِهِ، ومَنشأُ تلكَ النَّوَعِيَّةِ اتَّحادُ حقيقتِهِ في الأفراد، ولذلكَ سُمِّيَ بالحقيقي . (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى المَاهِيَّةِ الكُلِّيَّةِ المَقُوْلِ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا الجِنْسُ فِي جَوَابِ : مَا هُوَ؟ يخرج الجنس العالي الذي ليس فوقه جنس ، وَكَذَا الفصل والخاصَّةُ والعَرَضُ العام بالنّسبة إلى جنسِ الماهِيَّةِ، لكنَّ هذهِ الثَّلاثةَ بالنَّظر إلى أجناسِهَا ; أنواع إضافيَّةٌ، وكأنَّهُ ـ قُدِّسَ سِرُّهُ - لم يجعل هذا الكلام تعريفاً للنَّوعِ ؛ بل بياناً لِلحُكُم وإطلاقاً له، تلك
Chapter: On the Principles of Conceptualizations.
(And it may be said): means: just as the term 'species' is said of the mentioned meaning, so too the term 'species' is said of the universal essence that is predicated of itself and of other than itself: 'the genus', in answer to 'what is it?'
al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'And it may be said') 'qad' indicates rarity; i.e., it may be applied, and the word 'species' is used rarely. (His saying: 'predicated of itself and of other than itself the genus') excludes the highest genus, the simple species, and the species composed of two coextensive matters. Each of these three is not a relative species, because it is not said of it and of other than it a genus.
al-'Attar: ... (then continues from previous discussion, but here the text transitions to the next commentary). (His saying: 'And it may be said') i.e., it is applied and used, and he indicated by the word 'qad' that the use of 'species' in the first meaning is more frequent. It is called 'relative' because for its being a species it must be subsumed under a genus along with another species, so it is in reciprocal relation (mudaaf) with it. Thus the genus and the species subsumed under it are correlatives, like father and son. As for the reality of the real species, it is a relation and addition between it and its individuals; only the reality of its individuals is considered. And the source of that 'species-ness' is the unity of its reality in the individuals; therefore it is called 'real'. (His saying: 'upon the universal essence predicated of itself and of other than itself the genus in answer to what is it?') excludes the highest genus which has no genus above it, likewise the differentia, the property, and the common accident relative to the genus of the essence. But these three, with respect to their own genera, are relative species. It is as if he – sanctified his secret – did not make this statement a definition of species, but rather an explanation of the judgment and an application of it.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion on the concept of the relative species (al-naw' al-idafi). The matn states that the term 'species' can also be applied to a universal essence that is predicated of itself and of something else, and that something else is the genus in answer to 'what is it?' This is the relative species, as opposed to the real species. Al-Dasuqi's commentary explains that the particle 'qad' (قد) indicates that this usage is rare. He then identifies what is excluded by the condition 'predicated of itself and of other than itself a genus': it excludes the highest genus (which has no genus above it), the simple species (a species that has no coordinate species? Actually, he says the simple species and the species composed of two coextensive matters are not relative species because they cannot be predicated of themselves and of another genus). Then al-'Attar clarifies why it is called 'relative': because its species-ness depends on being subsumed under a genus alongside another species, creating a mutual relation. This contrasts with the real species, whose species-ness comes from the unity of reality in its individuals. He also notes that the differentia, property, and common accident, when considered relative to the genus of the essence, are not relative species, but when considered relative to their own genera, they are relative species. The author seems to intend an explanation of the judgment, not a strict definition.

النوع الإضافي
النوع الحقيقي
الجنس العالي
النوع البسيط

C) It has no genus above it.
D) It is composed of genus and differentia.

Key Takeaway
The relative species is defined by being predicated of itself and of another thing that is its genus, creating a correlative relation.

The Five Universals
intermediate

Exclusions from Relative Species
Author defines relative species and distinguishes it from absolute species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the categories that cannot be relative species and explain why each fails the condition.

Core Idea
The highest genus, simple species, and composed species are excluded because they are not predicated of themselves and of another genus.

Al-Dasuqi's commentary explicitly excludes three types of universals from being relative species. Understanding these exclusions deepens our grasp of the condition. Further, al-'Attar explains that even differentia, property, and common accident can be relative species when considered under their own genera.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three excluded categories
Al-Dasuqi says: 'It excludes the highest genus (al-jins al-'ali), the simple species (al-naw' al-basit), and the species composed of two coextensive matters (al-naw' al-murakkab min amrayn mutasawiyayn).'
These are not relative species because they do not satisfy the condition.
2
Understand why each fails
For each: The highest genus has no genus above it, so it cannot be predicated of a genus. The simple species (likely a species that is not built from genus and differentia) does not have a distinct genus to be predicated of. The composed species (e.g., 'rational animal' where the components are coextensive) cannot be predicated of a single genus because it is already a composite of two coextensive elements.
The text's reason is simple: 'because it is not said of it and of other than it a genus' (لا يُقالُ عليه وعلى غيره جنس).
3
Note the exception for differentia, property, and common accident
Al-'Attar points out that when considered relative to the genus of the essence (jins al-mahiyya), the differentia, property, and common accident are not relative species. However, relative to their own genera (i.e., the genera they fall under as species in a different hierarchy), they are relative species.
This shows that the category depends on the perspective of the hierarchy.
4
Summarize the condition for relative species
Only those universal essences that are predicated of themselves and of a genus above them can be called relative species. Anything that lacks a higher genus or is not predicated in that way is excluded.
This condition is essential for correct classification in definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات
(وَقَدْ يُقَالُ)؛ أي: كما يقالُ النَّوعُ على المعنى المذكور، كذلك يقال النَّوعُ عَلَى المَاهِيَّةِ الكُلِّيَّةِ المقُوْلِ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا: «الجِنْسُ»، فِي جَوَاب : مَا هُوَ؟
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ: وَقَدْ يُقَالُ) «قد» للتقليل ؛ أي: قد يُطلَقُ، ويحمل لفظ النَّوعِ بقلة . (قَوْلُهُ : الْمَقُوْلِ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا الْجِنْسُ خرج به الجنس العالي، والنَّوع البسيط، والنّوع المركَّب من أمرين متساويين، فكلُّ واحدٍ من هذه الثَّلاثةِ لا يكونُ نوعاً إضافيا ؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُقالُ عليه وعلى غيره جنس .
العطار
يصيرُ بِهِ مُمتازاً عَمَّا عداه، ثمَّ إِنَّ الأعراض اللاحقة للأشخاص؛ لَيسَتْ قائمةٌ بِهَا ، بل بموادّها، وإلا ; يلزمُ الدَّورُ ; لأنَّ الأعراضَ مُتشخّصةٌ بِمحالها، والحقُّ أَنَّ الوجود الخارجي هو المشخّصُ، وأمَّا الأعراض ; فَهيَ أمارات له، ويمكنُ أنْ ينبه عليهِ بأنَّ تمايزَ العَرَضَيْن المتماثلين ; يحصلُ مِن وجودِهِمَا في الموضوعين، و تمايز الصُّورتَين المتماثلتين يحصل مِن وجودِهِمَا في المادَّتَيْنِ، وقد تقرَّرَ في مَوضِعِهِ أنَّ وجودَ العَرَضِ ; هو بعينه وجوده في الموضوع , ووجودَ الصُّورة; هو بعينه وجودها في المادَّةِ فَتَفَطَّنْ، فإنَّهُ يحتاج إلى لُطفِ القريحة ا.هـ. (قَوْلُهُ : وَقَدْ يُقَالُ) أي : يطلقُ ويحملُ، وأشار بكلمة «قد» إلى أنَّ استعمال النَّوع بالمعنى الأوَّلِ أكثرُ ، وإِنَّما سُمِّيَ إضافيًّا ؛ لأَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ فِي نَوْعِيَّتِهِ مِن اندراجِهِ مِن نوع آخَرَ تحتَ جنسٍ، فيكون مُضايفاً له، فالجنس والنَّوعُ المندرج تحته مُتَضايفَانِ كالأب والابن وأمَّا نوعيَّةُ النّوع الحقيقيّ؛ فَهِيَ نِسبةٌ وإضافةٌ بينَهُ وبينَ أفراده، فليس يعتبر فيها إلا حقيقة أفرادِهِ، ومَنشأُ تلكَ النَّوَعِيَّةِ اتَّحادُ حقيقتِهِ في الأفراد، ولذلكَ سُمِّيَ بالحقيقي . (قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى المَاهِيَّةِ الكُلِّيَّةِ المَقُوْلِ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا الجِنْسُ فِي جَوَابِ : مَا هُوَ؟ يخرج الجنس العالي الذي ليس فوقه جنس ، وَكَذَا الفصل والخاصَّةُ والعَرَضُ العام بالنّسبة إلى جنسِ الماهِيَّةِ، لكنَّ هذهِ الثَّلاثةَ بالنَّظر إلى أجناسِهَا ; أنواع إضافيَّةٌ، وكأنَّهُ ـ قُدِّسَ سِرُّهُ - لم يجعل هذا الكلام تعريفاً للنَّوعِ ؛ بل بياناً لِلحُكُم وإطلاقاً له، تلك
Chapter: On the Principles of Conceptualizations.
(And it may be said): means: just as the term 'species' is said of the mentioned meaning, so too the term 'species' is said of the universal essence that is predicated of itself and of other than itself: 'the genus', in answer to 'what is it?'
al-Dasuqi: (His saying: 'And it may be said') 'qad' indicates rarity; i.e., it may be applied, and the word 'species' is used rarely. (His saying: 'predicated of itself and of other than itself the genus') excludes the highest genus, the simple species, and the species composed of two coextensive matters. Each of these three is not a relative species, because it is not said of it and of other than it a genus.
al-'Attar: ... (then continues from previous discussion, but here the text transitions to the next commentary). (His saying: 'And it may be said') i.e., it is applied and used, and he indicated by the word 'qad' that the use of 'species' in the first meaning is more frequent. It is called 'relative' because for its being a species it must be subsumed under a genus along with another species, so it is in reciprocal relation (mudaaf) with it. Thus the genus and the species subsumed under it are correlatives, like father and son. As for the reality of the real species, it is a relation and addition between it and its individuals; only the reality of its individuals is considered. And the source of that 'species-ness' is the unity of its reality in the individuals; therefore it is called 'real'. (His saying: 'upon the universal essence predicated of itself and of other than itself the genus in answer to what is it?') excludes the highest genus which has no genus above it, likewise the differentia, the property, and the common accident relative to the genus of the essence. But these three, with respect to their own genera, are relative species. It is as if he – sanctified his secret – did not make this statement a definition of species, but rather an explanation of the judgment and an application of it.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion on the concept of the relative species (al-naw' al-idafi). The matn states that the term 'species' can also be applied to a universal essence that is predicated of itself and of something else, and that something else is the genus in answer to 'what is it?' This is the relative species, as opposed to the real species. Al-Dasuqi's commentary explains that the particle 'qad' (قد) indicates that this usage is rare. He then identifies what is excluded by the condition 'predicated of itself and of other than itself a genus': it excludes the highest genus (which has no genus above it), the simple species (a species that has no coordinate species? Actually, he says the simple species and the species composed of two coextensive matters are not relative species because they cannot be predicated of themselves and of another genus). Then al-'Attar clarifies why it is called 'relative': because its species-ness depends on being subsumed under a genus alongside another species, creating a mutual relation. This contrasts with the real species, whose species-ness comes from the unity of reality in its individuals. He also notes that the differentia, property, and common accident, when considered relative to the genus of the essence, are not relative species, but when considered relative to their own genera, they are relative species. The author seems to intend an explanation of the judgment, not a strict definition.

Checkpoint
Why is the highest genus (al-jins al-'ali) not considered a relative species?
A) It has many species under it.
B) It is not a universal essence.
C) It has no genus above it to be predicated of.
D) It is a simple species.

Key Takeaway
The highest genus, simple species, and composed species are not relative species because they lack the required predicate relation to a genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Determine whether 'substance' (jawhar) is a relative species. If not, to which of the three excluded categories does it belong? Explain using the condition from al-Dasuqi's commentary.
?
Consider 'rationality' (al-nutq) as a differentia. According to al-'Attar, can 'rationality' ever be a relative species? If so, under what condition?

The Five Universals
intermediate
5 min
Defining the Relative Type and Its Conditions
Defines relative type as a universal quiddity predicated on itself and others by a genus in answer to 'what is it?'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a relative type and distinguish it from the real type and from subspecies using the definition's exclusions and the condition of 'primarily'.

Core Idea
The relative type is a universal quiddity predicated on itself and others by a genus, but only when predication is primary.

In this lesson, we examine the definition of the relative type as presented in the Tadhheeb. Unlike the real type, which derives its species-ness from the unity of essence across individuals, the relative type is defined by its subordination to a genus alongside another species. We will walk through the definition, its exclusions, and the necessary condition of 'primarily' to avoid including subspecies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and its genus
Find the term being defined (النوع الإضافي) and the genus used in its definition. The genus is the universal that is predicated on the type itself and on other things in answer to 'what is it?'.
For example, the genus of 'animal' is 'growing body'.
2
Extract the differentia
The key differentia is that the genus is predicated on the type itself and on other things. This sets the relative type apart from the real type, whose species-ness comes from unity of essence.
3
Apply the exclusions
The definition automatically excludes three categories: the highest genus (nothing predicated on it), the simple species (no genus), and the species composed of two coextensive parts (genus not predicated on it and others). Test why each fails.
E.g., 'substance' is a highest genus, so it cannot be a relative type.
4
Handle the subspecies (sinf) with the 'primarily' condition
A subspecies like 'Turk' (a human with an accidental property) would fall under the definition because its genus 'animal' is predicated on it and on a horse. To exclude it, add the condition that the predication must be 'primarily' (i.e., essential, not accidental).
The term 'primarily' ensures only essential predicates count.
