(قَوْلُهُ: الْمَقُوْلِ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا الْجِنْسُ خرج به الجنس العالي، والنَّوع البسيط، والنّوع المركَّب من أمرين متساويين، فكلُّ واحدٍ من هذه الثَّلاثةِ لا يكونُ نوعاً إضافيا؛ لأنَّهُ لا يُقالُ عليه وعلى غيره جنس. العطار يصيرُ بِهِ مُمتازاً عَمَّا عداه، ثمَّ إِنَّ الأعراض اللاحقة للأشخاص؛ لَيسَتْ قائمةٌ بِهَا، بل بموادّها، وإلا؛ يلزمُ الدَّورُ؛ لأنَّ الأعراضَ مُتشخّصةٌ بِمحالها، والحقُّ أَنَّ الوجود الخارجي هو المشخّصُ، وأمَّا الأعراض؛ فَهيَ أمارات له، ويمكنُ أنْ ينبه عليهِ بأنَّ تمايزَ العَرَضَيْن المتماثلين؛ يحصلُ مِن وجودِهِمَا في الموضوعين، و تمايز الصُّورتَين المتماثلتين يحصل مِن وجودِهِمَا في المادَّتَيْنِ، وقد تقرَّرَ في مَوضِعِهِ أنَّ وجودَ العَرَضِ؛ هو بعينه وجوده في الموضوع، ووجودَ الصُّورة؛ هو بعينه وجودها في المادَّةِ فَتَفَطَّنْ، فإنَّهُ يحتاج إلى لُطفِ القريحة ا.هـ. (قَوْلُهُ: وَقَدْ يُقَالُ) أي: يطلقُ ويحملُ، وأشار بكلمة «قد» إلى أنَّ استعمال النَّوع بالمعنى الأوَّلِ أكثرُ، وإِنَّما سُمِّيَ إضافيًّا؛ لأَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ فِي نَوْعِيَّتِهِ مِن اندراجِهِ مِن نوع آخَرَ تحتَ جنسٍ، فيكون مُضايفاً له، فالجنس والنَّوعُ المندرج تحته مُتَضايفان كالأب والابن وأمَّا نوعيَّةُ النّوع الحقيقيّ؛ فَهِيَ نِسبةٌ وإضافةٌ بينَهُ وبينَ أفراده، فليس يعتبر فيها إلا حقيقة أفرادِهِ، ومَنشأُ تلكَ النَّوَعِيَّةِ اتَّحادُ حقيقتِهِ في الأفراد، ولذلكَ سُمِّيَ بالحقيقي. (قَوْلُهُ: عَلَى المَاهِيَّةِ الكُلِّيَّةِ المَقُوْلِ عَلَيْهَا وَعَلَى غَيْرِهَا الجِنْسُ فِي جَوَابِ: مَا هُوَ؟ يخرج الجنس العالي الذي ليس فوقه جنس، وكَذَا الفصل والخاصَّةُ والعَرَضُ العام بالنّسبة إلى جنسِ الماهِيَّةِ، لكنَّ هذهِ الثَّلاثةَ بالنَّظر إلى أجناسِهَا؛ أنواع إضافيَّةٌ، وكأنَّهُ قُدِّسَ سِرُّهُ - لم يجعل هذا الكلام تعريفاً للنَّوعِ؛ بل بياناً لِلحُكُم وإطلاقاً له، (ثم قال) كالحيوان فإنَّه نوع بهذا التَّفسير؛ لأنَّ الجنس وهو الجسم النامي، عليه وعلى غيره من النباتات، وكذلك الجسمُ النَّامي نوع؛ الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ: كَالْحَيَوَانِ) أي: وكـ: (الشَّجر)، فهو نوع إضافي، فكلُّ مِنَ الحيوانِ والشَّجرِ؛ نوع إضافيّ؛ لأنَّ الجنس، وهو الجسمُ النَّامي، يُقالُ عليهما. (قَوْلُهُ: الْجِنْسُ) نائب فاعل المقول. (قَوْلُهُ: يُقَالُ عَلَيْهِ أي: على الجسمِ النَّامي، وقوله: (وعلى غيره)، وهو الجسم الغيرُ النَّامي كـ: (الحجر). (قَوْلُهُ: مِنَ النَّبَاتَاتِ كَ: الشَّجر. العطار وإلا؛ فيرد النَّقصُ بالصَّنْفِ، لكنَّ العبارة ظاهرة في التّعريف؛ قالَه شيخ الإسلام حفيد المصنّف، وقد تجاذب المحشَّيانِ أطراف هذه العبارة وتكلَّما فيها بما ستراه، وبعد أنْ أشرحَ لَكَ التَّعريفَ حَسبَمَا قرَّرَهُ مواد الأصل، والجلال أوقفَكَ على ما لهم هنا من التخليط في المقالِ، فَأَقولُ وبِاللهِ التَّوفيقُ: إِنَّ قولَهُ يُقالُ على الماهية ... إلخ، إنَّ لفظ الماهيَّة تستلزمُ الكُلِّيَّةَ؛ أي: الماهيَّةَ الكُلِّيَّةَ، فيخرج بذلكَ النَّشْخُصُ، وخرج الجنس العالي لِعَدَمِ مقوليَّة شيءٍ عليه، وخرجَ الفصلُ والخاصَّةُ والعرضُ العام بالنسبة إلى جنس الماهية، فإنَّ الجنس كالحيوان، مثلاً: وإنْ كانَ مقولاً على الفصل؛ كالنَّاطِقِ، وعلى الخاصَّةِ؛ كالضَّاحِكِ، وعلى العَرَضِ العام؛ كالماشي؛ لكن لا في جواب: ما هو؟ إذْ ليسَ الحيوان تمام المشترك، ولا ذاتيا، فهذهِ الثَّلاثَةُ، وإِنْ كَانَ مقولاً عليها وعلى غيرها الجنسُ؛ لكن لا في جواب ما هو، وأمَّا هذهِ الثَّلاثة بالنسبة إلى أجناسها الداخلة فيها؛ فإنَّها أنواعٌ إضافيَّةٌ، كما قاله المصنِّفُ في شرح الأصل، وذلك لما تقرَّرَ أنَّ الكُلِّيَّاتِ الخمسَ تُقالُ على حِصَصِهَا أيضاً، وتِلْكَ الحِصَصُ أنواع إضافيَّةٌ، وأمَّا الصِّنفُ الذي هو عبارةٌ عَنِ النَّوع المقيَّدِ بِقَيْدٍ عَرَضَيٌّ كُلِّيِّ كَالتركي؛ فَإِنَّهُ داخل تحتَ التَّعريف؛ لأنَّهُ يُقالُ عليه وعلى الفرس مَثلاً: الجنس الذي هو الحيوان في جوابِ ما هو، فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ إخراجه بزيادة قيد وهو: قولاً أوليا؛ فإنَّهُ، وإِنْ قِيلَ عليهِ
CHAPTER: On the principles of concepts. (And it may be said): i.e., just as the word 'species' is used for the previously mentioned meaning, likewise 'species' is used for the universal quiddity which is predicated on itself and on other things: 'the genus', in answer to 'what is it?' Al-Desouqi: (His statement: 'And it may be said') 'qad' indicates infrequency; i.e., the word 'species' is sometimes used, though rarely. (His statement: 'predicated on itself and on other things the genus' excludes the highest genus, the simple species, and the species composed of two coextensive things; each of these three is not a relative species because a genus is not predicated on it and on other things. Al-Attar: It becomes distinguished from others by it; then the accidents that affect individuals are not subsistent in them, but in their matters; otherwise, circularity would arise, because accidents are individuated by their loci. The truth is that external existence is the individuator, while accidents are mere signs for it. One can also point out that the differentiation of two similar accidents occurs through their existence in two subjects, and the differentiation of two similar forms occurs through their existence in two matters. It has been established in its place that the existence of an accident is identical to its existence in the subject, and the existence of a form is identical to its existence in matter. So be perceptive, for it requires subtle intelligence. End. (His statement: 'And it may be said') i.e., it is used and applied. He indicated by 'qad' that the use of 'species' in the first sense is more frequent. It is called 'relative' because its species-ness necessarily involves its falling under a genus along with another species, so it is related to it; thus genus and the species falling under it are correlatives like father and son. As for the species-ness of the real species, it is a relation and addition between it and its individuals, so only the reality of its individuals is considered in it, and the origin of that species-ness is the unity of its reality in the individuals; therefore it is called 'real'. (His statement: 'the universal quiddity which is predicated on itself and on other things the genus in answer to: what is it?' excludes the highest genus which has no genus above it, and likewise the differentia, the property, and the general accident relative to the genus of the quiddity; but these three, in relation to their own genera, are relative species. It is as if he—may his secret be sanctified—did not make this statement a definition of 'species' but rather a clarification of the ruling and its application. (Then he said): Like 'animal', for it is a species according to this interpretation, because the genus, which is 'growing body', is predicated on it and on other things like plants; likewise 'growing body' is a species. Al-Desouqi: (His statement: 'like animal') i.e., and like 'tree', for it is a relative species. So each of 'animal' and 'tree' is a relative species because the genus, i.e., 'growing body', is predicated on both. (His statement: 'the genus') is the subject of the passive participle 'predicated'. (His statement: 'predicated on it') i.e., on 'growing body'; and his statement: 'and on other things', i.e., the non-growing body like 'stone'. (His statement: 'from plants like tree'. Al-Attar: Otherwise, the defect of the 'subspecies' would come in, but the expression is apparent as a definition; so said Shaykh al-Islam, the grandson of the author. The two glossators have debated the aspects of this expression and spoken about it such that you will see. After I explain the definition to you according to what the materials of the original text have established, and al-Jalal has made you aware of what confusion they have here in the discourse, I say—and with God is success: Indeed, his statement 'said of the quiddity... etc.'—the term 'quiddity' implies universality; i.e., the universal quiddity, thus the individual is excluded. Also excluded is the highest genus for lack of anything being predicated on it; and excluded are the differentia, the property, and the general accident relative to the genus of the quiddity. For instance, the genus 'animal', though it is predicated on the differentia like 'rational', on the property like 'laughing', and on the general accident like 'walking', but not in answer to 'what is it?' because 'animal' is neither the complete commonality nor an essential. So these three, even if the genus is predicated on them and on others, they are not in answer to 'what is it?'. As for these three in relation to their own genera that fall under them, they are relative species, as the author said in the commentary on the original text. And that is because it has been established that the five universals are also predicated on their subcategories, and those subcategories are relative species. As for the 'subspecies' which is the species restricted by a universal accidental condition like 'Turk', it falls under the definition because the genus 'animal' is predicated on it and on a horse, for example, in answer to 'what is it?'. So it must be excluded by adding a condition: 'primarily', for even though it is predicated on it...
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage defines the relative type (al-naw‘ al-idaafi) as one of the applications of the term 'type' in logic. The author begins by stating that, in addition to the real type (al-naw‘ al-haqiqi) defined earlier, the term 'type' can also be used for a universal quiddity that is predicated on itself and on other things by a genus in answer to 'what is it?'. This is the relative type. The commentators clarify that the word 'qad' indicates this usage is less frequent. Al-Desouqi explains that this definition excludes three things: the highest genus (which has no genus above it), the simple species (which has no genus), and the species composed of two coextensive parts (like 'rational animal' which is a species but not relative because its genus is not predicated on it and on others—since it is identical to its genus in extension). Al-Attar then offers a digression on individuation, but the main thread continues: the relative type is so-called because its species-ness requires it to fall under a genus alongside another species, making it correlative to that genus, like father and son. The real type, by contrast, derives its species-ness from the unity of its essence across individuals. The author then provides examples: 'animal' is a relative type because its genus 'growing body' is predicated on it and on plants; similarly 'growing body' is a relative type because its genus 'body' is predicated on it and on non-growing bodies like stones. Al-Attar later addresses a potential confusion: the 'subspecies' (al-sinf), which is a type restricted by an accidental condition (e.g., 'Turk' meaning a human who is Turkish), falls under the definition because 'animal' is predicated on it and on a horse in answer to 'what is it?'. To exclude it, one must add that the predication should be 'primarily' (qawlan awwaliyyan), meaning essential predication without accidental restriction. This preserves the precision of the definition.

Key Terms
نوع إضافي
جنس عالي
صنف
كلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a relative type (naw‘ idaafi)?
A) The highest genus, such as 'substance'
B) The species 'animal', because its genus 'growing body' is predicated on it and on plants
C) The differentia 'rational'
D) An individual person like Zayd

Key Takeaway
The relative type is defined by the predication of its genus on itself and others in answer to 'what is it?', but must be distinguished from subspecies by the condition of primary predication.

Resolving Overlap in Species Naming: Haqiqi and Idafi
Commentary resolving an objection about naming species types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to resolve the apparent contradiction between the specific naming of species types and their potential overlap by applying the concept of restriction on the name.

Core Idea
A species named 'real' can also be 'relative' — naming restricts the term, not the thing.

In logic, species are divided into real (haqiqi) and relative (idafi). But what happens when the same entity can be called both? This passage from a commentary on al-Tadhheeb addresses precisely that objection. It shows that the specificity of naming does not prevent a species from being described by another name when viewed from a different perspective. Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two species and their names
Find in the Arabic where 'al-naw' al-haqiqi' (real species) and 'al-naw' al-idafi' (relative species) are mentioned. Understand that the relative species is defined by its relation to what is above it (its genus), while the real species is ultimate.
The relative species example: 'animal' is a species in relation to 'body'. Real species example: 'human' is a species of nothing else.
2
Understand the objection about overlap
Al-Dasuqi points out that if each type has a specific name, this conflicts with the fact that there is a relation of 'general and particular from one perspective' (عموم وخصوص من وجه) between them. This means they can overlap—something could be both a real and a relative species. How can one thing have two exclusive names?
3
Analyse the solution: restriction on the name
The answer is that specifying each type with a name (e.g., 'real') restricts the name to that type, but does not prevent the same thing from being called by the other name (e.g., 'relative') when considered from another angle. The restriction is on the name, not on the entity.
The summary explains: 'the ba' enters on the restricted, and the restricted is only the naming... the restriction of this naming to it does not prevent it being named by another name.'
4
Distinguish real relative from well-known relative
Al-Attar clarifies that the relation between species and genus is a 'well-known relative' (mudaf mashhuri), not a real ontological relative. The real relative here is the predicative relation: genus predicated of species in answer to 'what is it?' and vice versa.
This distinction prevents confusion between logical relations and real relations in ontology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُخصُّ هَذَا النَّوْعُ بِاسْم الإِضَافِيّ) ، فإِنَّ نوعِيَّته بالإضافة إلى ما فوقه. الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ: وَيُخَصُ . . . إِلَخ) فيه : أنَّ كونَ كلِّ مِنَ النَّوعَيْنِ مُختصّا باسم يُنافي أن يكون بينهما عموم وخصوص من وجه؛ لأنَّهما على هذا يجتمعان، ويُطلق على الذي اجتمع؛ إضافي وحقيقي. وأُجيب : بأنَّ تخصيص كلِّ مِنَ النَّوعيين باسم؛ لا ينافي تسميته بآخر. (۱) وحاصله : أنَّ الباء داخلة على المقصور، والمقصورُ إِنَّما هو التّسمية بالجنس على الأوَّلِ؛ لا العكس(٢)، وقصرُ هذه التسمية عليهِ لا يُنافي أنَّه يُسمَّى بغيرِ هذا الاسم أيضاً، وَكَذَا يُقالُ في الثَّاني. العطار (قَوْلُهُ : بِاسْم الْإِضَافِيّ) أقحم لفظ اسم الإشارة إلى أنَّ المجموع هو الاسم. (قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنَّ نَوْعِيَّتَهُ بِالْإِضَافَةِ لِمَا فَوْقَهُ فَهُمَا مُتَضايفان مشهوريَّانِ؛ عرضَ لهما المضافانِ الحقيقيَّانِ، وهوَ كَوْنُ الجنسِ مَقولاً عليه في جواب مَا هُوَ، وكُونُهُ مَقولاً عليه الجنس في جواب مَا هوَ؟ والفرقُ بين المضاف الحقيقي والمضاف المشهوري؛ بَيَّنَّاه في حواشي المقولاتِ الكُبرى.
And this type is specified by the name 'al-idafi' (relative), for its specificity lies in its relation to what is above it. al-Dasuqi (his saying: 'And it is specified... etc.'): In this there is that the fact that each of the two types is specifically named conflicts with there being a general-and-particular from one perspective between them, because by this they come together, and what comes together is called both relative and real. It was answered: that the specific naming of each of the two types does not prevent its being named by another. (1) The summary is that the ba' (preposition) enters on the restricted (maqsur), and the restricted is only the naming by the genus in the first, not the reverse, and the restriction of this naming to it does not prevent it being named by another name as well. Similarly is said in the second. al-Attar (his saying: 'by the name al-idafi'): He inserted the word 'isim' (name) to indicate that the composite is the name. (His saying: 'for its specificity is by relation to what is above it, so they are two well-known relatives; they are accompanied by two real relatives, which are that the genus is predicated of it in answer to 'what is it?', and that it is predicated of the genus in answer to 'what is it?'. The difference between the real relative and the well-known relative we have explained in the glosses on the greater categories.)
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary on the classification of species into two types: real (haqiqi) and relative (idafi). It begins by quoting a statement: 'And this type is specified by the name 'al-idafi'' and explains that the specificity of the relative species lies in its relation to the genus above it. al-Dasuqi raises an objection: if each type has its own specific name, this seems to conflict with the fact that there can be a relationship of 'general and particular from one perspective' (عموم وخصوص من وجه) between them, meaning they can overlap. In such overlap, the same entity could be called both real and relative. The answer given is that specifying each type with a name does not prevent it from also being called by the other name. The summary explains that the preposition 'ba' in 'specified by the name' indicates that the restriction (qasr) is on the name itself, not on the entity being named. For example, the name 'real' is restricted to the real species, but that does not prevent the real species from also being called 'relative' when considered from another perspective. Similarly, the relative species can be called 'real' under certain aspects. al-Attar then comments that the author inserted the word 'name' to clarify that the composite term (e.g., 'al-naw' al-idafi') is the name itself, not just the adjective. He further explains that the relativity is a 'well-known relative' (al-mudaf al-mashhuri) as opposed to a 'real relative' (al-mudaf al-haqiqi). The real relative here is the relationship of predication: the genus is predicated of the species in answer to 'what is it?', and the species is predicated of the genus in answer to 'what is it?' (the latter being a way to define the genus's inferior). The difference between these two types of relatives is said to have been explained elsewhere. This passage thus details the terminological precision required in naming logical categories.

النوع الحقيقي
المضاف المشهوري
المضاف الحقيقي
عموم وخصوص من وجه
القصر

A) Because the names are ambiguous
B) Because the restriction is on the name, not on the thing named
C) Because the species types are mutually exclusive
D) Because the author made a mistake

Key Takeaway
The specific naming of species does not preclude alternative descriptions; the key is that the restriction is on the name, not the entity.

When a Name Binds Too Tightly: Objection and Answer on al-Naw' al-Haqiqi and al-Idafi
Hashiya raises objection about naming conflict and answers it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical relationship between al-naw' al-haqiqi and al-naw' al-idafi and evaluate the objection regarding their naming as a category mistake.

Core Idea
A name specifies but does not exhaust—two types can share instances without conflict.

This hashiv passage tackles a subtle but crucial point: if each type (haqiqi and idafi) is assigned a unique name, how can they have a relationship of 'umum wa khusus min wajh (generality and specificity in some respect)? The objection seems compelling, but the answer reveals a distinction between the name and the named entity. Mastering this distinction will sharpen your ability to handle overlapping categories in Islamic logic and usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core objection
The objector claims that if each type (al-naw' al-haqiqi and al-naw' al-idafi) is specified by a unique name, they cannot have a 'umum wa khusus min wajh relationship. Why? Because that relationship requires them to apply to the same instance, which would then have two names, contradicting the specification.
The objection assumes that a unique name means exclusive application.
2
Recognize the logical relationship at stake
The 'umum wa khusus min wajh relationship means two terms overlap in some cases but differ in others. For example, 'insan' (human) is a haqiqi type, but it can also be considered idafi when compared to a broader genus like 'hayawan'. They share instances like 'Zayd'.
Understanding this overlap is key to seeing why the objection fails.
3
Analyze the solution's key move
The answer distinguishes between the name (ism) and the named (musamma). Specifying a name for a type does not prevent that type from being called by another name from a different perspective. The preposition 'ba' in the original phrase indicates that the limitation (qasr) is on the naming itself, not on the entity. So naming something 'haqiqi' does not stop it from also being called 'idafi' when considered relationally.
This is a classic move: don't confuse a linguistic restriction with an ontological one.
4
Apply the distinction to avoid similar confusions
In Islamic sciences, terms like 'farḍ' and 'wājib' in Hanafi fiqh are technically distinct but overlap in many rulings. If one insists each has a unique name, they might wrongly think they cannot apply to the same act. The hashiv's resolution shows that naming is flexible; what matters is the aspect under consideration.
Use this to analyze other pairs of overlapping terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ: وَيُخَصُّ ... إِلَخ فيه: أنَّ كونَ كلِّ مِنَ النَّوعَيْنِ مُختصّا باسم يُنافي أن يكون بينهما عموم وخصوص من وجه؛ لأنَّهما على هذا يجتمعان، ويُطلق على الذي اجتمع إضافي وحقيقي. وأُجيب: بأنَّ تخصيص كلِّ مِنَ النَّوعيين باسم لا ينافي تسميته بآخر. وحاصله: أنَّ الباء داخلة على المقصور، والمقصور إنما هو التسمية بالجنس على الأوَّل لا العكس، وقصر هذه التسمية عليه لا يُنافي أنَّه يُسمَّى بغير هذا الاسم أيضاً، وكذا يُقال في الثاني.
His statement: 'and this type is specified by the name al-idafi' ... contains [the objection] that the fact that each of the two types is specified by a name contradicts their having generality and specificity in some respect, because on this basis they would combine, and the combination would be called both idafi and haqiqi. And it was answered: specifying each of the two types by a name does not preclude it from being named by another. The summary: the ba' enters upon the limited [term], and the limitation is only of the naming by genus in the first, not the reverse; restricting this naming to it does not prevent it from being called by another name as well, and similarly for the second.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) addressing an objection raised against the distinction between al-naw' al-haqiqi (real type) and al-naw' al-idafi (relational type). The objection states: if each type is specified by a unique name (e.g., 'insan' for haqiqi, 'animal' as idafi), then they cannot have a relationship of 'generality and specificity in some respect' because that relationship would require them to apply to the same thing, which would then have two names, contradicting the specification. The answer clarifies that specifying a name does not prevent the same thing from having another name. The explanation adds that the preposition 'ba' in the original phrase indicates the limited term (al-maqsūr) is the naming itself, not the named entity. Thus, restricting the naming 'haqiqi' to a specific type does not stop that type from also being called 'idafi' from another perspective. This resolves the apparent contradiction, allowing the two types to share instances.

النوع الحقيقي

Key Takeaway
Specifying a name for a logical type does not conflict with that type also being called by another name, because naming is a limitation on the description, not on the essence.

Real and Relational Types in Islamic Logic
Author defines the two types and explains their mutual relation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a real type (al-naw' al-haqiqi) and a relational type (al-naw' al-idafi) and identify their overlap in a given example.

Core Idea
A type can be both real and relational depending on perspective.

This passage introduces two foundational types used in Islamic logic: the real type, whose essence is identical across individuals, and the relational type, considered relative to a higher genus. Understanding their relationship is crucial for accurate definition and classification in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining feature of the real type
Find in the passage how the real type is defined: it is called al-haqiqi because its type-ness is based on its essence being unified in all its individuals. For example, every human shares the same rational animal essence.
2
Identify the defining feature of the relational type
The relational type is not fully defined here, but from context it is a type considered in relation to a higher genus. For example, 'animal' is a relational type when considered under 'living being'.
The passage focuses on the relationship, not the full definition.
3
Examine the example of 'insan'
The passage states that both types apply to 'insan'. 'Insan' is a real type in itself (its essence is unified), and it is also a relational type when considered under a higher genus like 'animal'. Thus, the two types coincide in this individual.
4
Understand the relationship of 'generality and specificity in some respect'
This logical relationship means that the two types have overlapping instances (like 'insan') but also instances where only one applies. For example, 'living being' is not a real type in the same sense as 'human', but it is a relational type. Practice applying this to other concepts.
This relationship is common in Islamic logic for comparing terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات. (كَالأَوَّلِ) أي كالنوع الأوَّل، فإنَّه يُخَصُّ بالحقيقي؛ لأنَّ نوعيَّتَه بالنظر إلى حقيقتِه المتَّحِدَةِ في أفرادِه. (وَبَيْنَهُمَا) أي بين النوعين (عُمُومٌ وخصوص من وجه) لتصادقهما على الإنسان.
Chapter: On the principles of concepts. (Like the first) i.e., like the first type, for it is specified by [the name] al-haqiqi because its being a type is by consideration of its essence that is unified in its individuals. (And between them) i.e., between the two types, (there is generality and specificity in some respect) because they both apply to 'insan'.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion from the sharh. It begins a new chapter titled 'On the Principles of Concepts.' The commentator clarifies that the first type (al-naw' al-awwal) is called al-naw' al-haqiqi (real type) because its type-ness is based on its essence being identical in all its individuals. For example, 'insan' (human) is a real type because every human shares the same rational animal essence. Then it states that between this real type and the relational type (al-naw' al-idafi) there is a relationship of generality and specificity in some respect (ʿumūm wa khuṣūṣ min wajh). This means they coincide in some instances but differ in others. The specific example given is that both types apply to 'insan': 'insan' is a real type in itself, and it is also a relational type when considered under a higher genus like 'animal'. Thus, the two types are not mutually exclusive but have overlapping extensions.

The real type and relational type are not mutually exclusive; they can coexist in the same concept from different perspectives, as illustrated by 'insan'.

Distinction between Real and Relative Species
Commentators explain the relationship between real and relative species with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given species in an Islamic science text is a real species or a relative species based on the criteria of subsumption under a genus and the nature of its individuals.

Core Idea
A real species is defined by its own essence; a relative species is defined by its subordination to a higher genus.

In Islamic logic, the classification of species is crucial for constructing precise definitions. This passage from the Tadhheeb Sharh explains that a species can be real when it is directly predicated of individuals of agreed essence, or relative when it is subsumed under a higher genus. For example, 'man' is both real and relative depending on the perspective. Understanding this distinction helps you evaluate definitions in Fiqh and Kalam with greater accuracy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the species term
Locate the species name in the passage (e.g., 'animal', 'point', 'man'). This is the term whose classification you need to determine.
2
Check for subsumption under a higher genus
Determine if the species is said to be subsumed under another genus. If the text states that it has a higher genus above it, it is likely a relative species.
For example, animal is subsumed under 'body' or 'living being'; man is subsumed under 'animal'.
3
Examine the nature of its individuals
Are the individuals of this species of agreed essence? For a real species, all individuals share the same essential definition. For a relative species, the 'individuals' are themselves species (subordinate types).
Point has individuals like 'end of line' and 'center' that share the same essence of being a point; animal has individuals like 'man', 'horse' which are different species.
4
Apply the definition criteria
Use the definitions: real species has individuals of agreed essence and is not subsumed under a genus as a subordinate; relative species is subsumed under a higher genus and its 'individuals' are species.
5
Test with examples
Apply to the examples given: animal is relative, point is real, man is both in different respects. Verify that the classification matches the criteria.

المتحدة فيها .
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ: بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَى حَقِيْقَتِهِ الْمُتَّحِدَةِ فِي أَفْرَادِهِ) أَشَارَ بِلفظ الأفرادِ إلى أنَّ المقصودَ هَهُنا ؛ بيانُ النِّسبةِ بينَهُما باعتبار الأفراد الحقيقية دون الحصص الاعتبارية، كما أنَّ المقصود من بيانِ النَّسَبِ الأربع المذكورة؛ كانَ ذلكَ، فَكَوْنُ كُلِّ كُلِّيِّ نوعاً حقيقيا بالقياس إلى حِصَصِهِ؛ لا يقدح في النّسبة المذكورة؛ فَلَا وَجْهَ لِمَا يُقالُ : إِنَّ كُلَّ كُلّيّ لَهُ أفراد في نفسِ الأمرِ ، فهو نوع حقيقي بالقياس إلى حِصَصِهِ، فلا يُتصوَّرُ صدقُ النَّوع الإضافي بدونِ الحقيقي أصلاً.
(قَوْلُهُ : لِتَصَادُقِهما ) أشار بِهِ إلى أنَّ النِّسبة مأخوذة باعتبارِ الصِّدق؛ أي: الحمل، وإلا ؛ فَمافهومَاهُمَا مُتبايِنَانِ .
(1) (قَوْلُهُ : وأقول ... إلخ) هذا جواب آخر بتصحيح جعل الباء داخلة على المقصور عليه. وحاصله أنهما في الاجتماع قد اتحدا ذاتاً واختلفا اعتباراً، فالإنسان من جهة اندراجه تحت غيره كالحيوان نوع إضافي فقط، ومن جهة اندراج جزئياته الحقيقية تحته حقيقي فقط . ا . هـ .
الشَّرنوبي .

فإنَّه يصدُقُ عليه النَّوعُ الحقيقي والإضافي، كما يظهر بأدنى تأمل. (وَتَفَارُقِهما ) بالجرّ عطف على قوله : «تصادقهما»؛ أي: لتفارُقِ النَّوعين (فِي الْحَيَوَانِ وَالنُّقْطَةِ، فإنَّ الحيوان نوعٌ إضافي لا حقيقي، والنُّقطة بالعكس؛ لأنَّها لو كانَتْ إضافيَّةٌ ؛ لاندرجت تحت جنس، فلا
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهِ النَّوْعُ الْحَقِيقِيُّ) أي: بالنَّظرِ لأفراده من زيد ونحوه، والإضافي : بالنظر للحيوان.
(قَوْلُهُ : وَالنُّقْطَةُ بِالْعَكْسِ أي : فهي نوع حقيقي؛ لَا إضافي؛ لأنَّها تصدقُ على أفرادٍ مُتَّفقةِ الحقيقة؛ كآخر هذا الخطّ، وآخر هذا الخط، وليست مندرجةً تحت جنس الذي هو ضابط الحقيقي . واعلَمْ (١) أنَّ التُقطةً يصدقُ عليها الوحدة وليس كلُّ وحدةٍ نُقطة، والنُّقطة وإن دخلَتْ تحتَ العَرَض ؛ لكنَّ العَرَضَ ليسَ جنساً لِمَا تحته ؛ لأنَّ العَرَضَ ؛ مَقوليتُهُ على ما تحته بالتّشكيكِ والجنس يجب أن تكونَ مَقوليّتُهُ على ما تحتَهُ بالتَّواطؤ .
العطار
هي
(قَوْلُهُ : وَالنُّقْطَةِ) ومثلها العقل والوحدة، وصحَّةُ التَّمثيل بِها ؛ يتوقَّفُ على أنَّ أفرادها مُتفقةُ الحقيقة، وعدم دخولها تحتَ مَقولةٍ مِنَ المقولات العشرِ ؛ فَيُقالُ في الأفرادِ الَّتي تحتَ مَفهوم النُّقطة، وهِيَ النُّقطةُ الَّتِي هِيَ طرفُ الخطِّ ، والنُّقطة التي هِيَ طرفُ سطح المخروط، والنُّقطة التي تعرضُ وسط الخط، ونقطة المركز؛ أنَّها أفرادٌ شَخصيَّةٌ، فلو مُجعِلَتْ أنواعاً مُندرجةً تحتَ جنس ؛ لم يصحَ التَّمثيل، ومثلُهُ في أفراد العقول العشرة، والوحدة تحتها الوحدةُ الشَّخصيَّةُ والنَّوعيَّةُ والجنسيّة والعَرَضيَّةُ والاتصالية والاجتماعية والاعتبارية. (قَوْلُهُ: لِأَنَّهَا لَوْ كَانَتْ إِضَافِيَّةٌ، لَانْدَرَجَتْ تَحْتَ جِنْسِ والتّالي باطل، والملازمة ظاهرةٌ، وأمَّا بيان بطلانِ التَّالي ؛ فَقَولُهُ: فَلَا تكون بسيطةٌ ; فَإِنَّهُ إِشارةٌ
يُقالُ
(۱) (قَوْلُهُ : واعلم ... إلخ) أي: فبينهما العموم والخصوص المطلق، تنفرد الوحدة عنها وحدة الشخص كزيد، ووحدة النوع كإنسان ووحدة الجنس ،كحيوان، ولا تنفرد النقطة عن الوحدة، وكلاهما نوع حقيقي لا غير . ا . هـ. الشَّرنوبي.
Section: On the principles of concepts.
(Like the first): i.e., like the first species, for it is specified as 'real' because its species-ness is by consideration of its essence united in its individuals.
(And between them) i.e., between the two species (there is general and specific in some respect) because they both apply to 'man'.
Al-Dasuqi: And I say in reply: The specification of naming as 'relative' is due to its being subsumed under another, and the specification of naming as 'real' is due to the subsumption of individuals of agreed essence under it. Therefore, it is possible for them to unite such that one thing is real in one respect and relative in another.
(His statement: 'by addition' i.e., by relation; i.e., due to its addition and relation to what is above it. (His statement: 'like the first') i.e., just as the first is specified by the name 'real', this is the meaning of the phrase. (His statement: 'to its essence united in its individuals') i.e., by consideration of it being the essence of all its individuals that are united in it.
Al-Attar: (His statement: 'by consideration of its essence united in its individuals') He indicated by the word 'individuals' that the intent here is the explanation of the relation between them by consideration of real individuals, not notional shares. As the intent of the explanation of the four mentioned relations was that. So every universal being a real species in relation to its shares does not harm the mentioned relation. Thus there is no basis for what is said: Every universal has individuals in reality, so it is a real species in relation to its shares, so the applicability of the relative species without the real is unimaginable.
(His statement: 'because they both apply') He indicated by this that the relation is taken by consideration of truth/application i.e., predication; otherwise their concepts are mutually exclusive.
(1) (His statement: 'And I say... etc.') This is another answer by correcting the inclusion of the preposition on the restricted. Its gist is that in their conjunction they have united in essence and differed in consideration. So man, from the aspect of his being subsumed under another like animal, is only a relative species, and from the aspect of the subsumption of his real particulars under him, is only a real species. End.
Al-Sharnubi.

For real species and relative species apply to him, as appears with minimal reflection. (And their distinction) in the genitive, coordinated with his statement 'their common applicability'; i.e., due to the distinction of the two species (in 'animal' and 'point'. For animal is a relative species, not real, and the point is the opposite; because if it were relative, it would be subsumed under a genus, then it would not be simple).
Al-Dasuqi: (His statement: 'For real species applies to him') i.e., by consideration of his individuals like Zayd etc., and the relative by consideration of animal.
(His statement: 'and the point is the opposite') i.e., it is a real species, not relative; because it applies to individuals of agreed essence like the end of one line and the end of another line, and it is not subsumed under a genus which is the condition for the relative. And know that the point has unity applying to it, but not every unity is a point. And the point, even if it falls under accident, yet accident is not a genus for what is under it; because accident is predicated of what is under it by analogy (tashkik), while genus must be predicated of what is under it by univocity (tawatu').
Al-Attar: (His statement: 'and the point') and similar to it are intellect and unity. The validity of the example with it depends on its individuals being of agreed essence and not falling under any of the ten categories. So it is said about the individuals under the concept of point, which are the point that is the end of the line, the point that is the end of the conical surface, the point that occurs in the middle of the line, and the point of the center: that they are individual persons. If they were made types subsumed under a genus, the example would not be valid. Similarly for the individuals of the ten intellects, and unity under which are personal unity, specific unity, generic unity, accidental unity, continuity unity, social unity, and conventional unity. (His statement: 'because if it were relative, it would be subsumed under a genus' and the consequent is false, the implication is apparent. As for the explanation of the falsity of the consequent: his statement: 'then it would not be simple').
(1) (His statement: 'and know... etc.') i.e., between them there is absolute general and specific. Unity is distinguished from it by personal unity like Zayd, specific unity like man, and generic unity like animal. And the point is not distinguished from unity, and both are real species only. End. Al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from the Tadhheeb Sharh explaining the distinction between two types of species in logic: real species (al-naw' al-haqiqi) and relative species (al-naw' al-idafi). The discussion begins by clarifying the definition: a real species is one whose species-ness is considered by its essence that is shared among its individuals uniformly, while a relative species is one that is subsumed under a higher genus. The commentators point out that these two types can coexist in the same thing under different considerations. For example, 'man' (al-insan) is both a real species when considered in relation to individual humans like Zayd, and a relative species when considered as subsumed under 'animal'. This is because the relationship between them is one of commonality and difference in some respect (umum wa khhusus min wajh). They illustrate this with the logical relations of common applicability (tasadiq) and distinct application (tafarruq). The text then gives examples: 'animal' is only a relative species because it has no individuals of agreed essence (its individuals are species like man, horse), while 'point' (al-nuqta) is only a real species because its individuals (e.g., the end of a line, the center of a circle) share the same essence and it is not subsumed under any genus. The commentator al-Attar elaborates that the point is not under a genus because it belongs to the category of accident, but accident is predicated by analogy (tashkik), not univocally (tawatu'), so it cannot serve as a genus. Furthermore, the example of unity (al-wahda) is discussed: unity is a real species with many subtypes (personal, specific, generic, etc.), and it also applies to the point but not vice versa. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that every universal with individuals must be a real species; rather, the distinction depends on the nature of the individuals and the mode of predication.

النوع الحقيقي
النوع الإضافي
التصادق
التواطؤ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a relative species (naw' idafi)?
A) Man (al-insan) when considered in relation to individual humans like Zayd
B) Animal (al-hayawan) when considered as subsuming man, horse, etc.
C) Point (al-nuqta) when considered as the end of a line
D) Unity (al-wahda) when considered as personal unity

Key Takeaway
The classification of a species as real or relative depends on whether its species-ness is based on its own essence or on its subordination to a higher genus, and this distinction is vital for accurate definitions in Islamic sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the definition of 'salah' (prayer) in Islamic law: 'specific actions and recitations beginning with takbir and ending with taslim.' Is 'salah' a real species or a relative species? Explain using the criteria from this lesson.
?
Consider the term 'nabidh' (date drink). In a hadith, it is sometimes considered under the genus of 'intoxicants'. Is 'nabidh' a real species or a relative species in that context?

True Species vs Relative Species: The Point as a Case Study
Commentary distinguishes true and relative species using animal and point.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a true species from a relative species using the example of the point (nuqta) and justify why the point is a true species.

Core Idea
A true species has individuals agreeing in essence and is not subsumed under a genus.

The distinction between true (haqiqi) and relative (idafi) species is crucial for understanding how universals classify realities. In this lesson, we explore the commentator's argument that the point (nuqta) is a true species because its individuals—like endpoints of different lines—share the same essence, unlike 'animal' which is a relative species when predicated of humans. We will dissect the criteria for a true species and test them against the point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two species types
Find where the commentator states that animal is a relative species and the point is a true species. Note the criteria: relative species is subsumed under a higher genus; true species is not.
The codex uses 'al-naw' al-haqiqi' and 'al-naw' al-idafi'.
2
Extract the defining mark of a true species
The commentator says the point's individuals 'agree in essence' (muttafiqat al-haqiqa) and it is not under a genus. This is the core of a true species.
3
Apply to the point's individuals
List the examples given: end of a line, end of a cone surface, middle of a line, center. Verify they share the same essence of being a point.
These are personal instances (afrad shakhsiyya), not types.
4
Contrast with animal as relative species
Animal is predicated of humans relative to a higher genus (e.g., living body). It is not a true species for humans because it is itself a genus for lower species.
Animal is al-naw' al-idafi when considered under a higher genus.

(قَوْلُهُ : هَذَا خُلْفٌ) أي : كونها غير بسيطةٍ ؛ خُلْف؛ أي : مطروح وراء الخلف؛ لكونها بسيطة . وفيه : أَنَّهُ إنْ أرادَ بسيطةٌ خارجاً ؛ فمُسلَّم، ولكن لا يضرنَا، وإنْ أراد عقلاً ؛ فَلَا ؛ لأنَّها نهاية الخط، فهي مُركَّبةٌ مُقيَّدةٌ بكونها نهاية الخطّ ؛ أي : إِنَّهَا مُركَّبَةٌ مِن مُطلقِ النّهايةِ، وَمِنْ هذا القيد، تأمل.
العطار
هي
لقياس مطوي تقريره : لو اندرجت تحت جنس لم تكن بسيطة، والتّالي باطل؛ لأنَّهُ خلافُ المفروض، لا يُقالُ : مُندرجةٌ تحتَ العَرَضِ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : ليس هو جنساً عالياً لِمَا تحتَهُ مِنَ المقولات؛ لأنَّه ليس ذاتيا لها، قال في شرح المقاصد: المعنى مِنَ الجوهر؛ ذاتُ الشَّيء وحقيقته، فيكون ذاتيًا بِخِلافِ العَرض فإنَّ معناه ما يعرضُ للموضوع، وعروضُ الشَّيءِ لِلشَّيء إِنَّما يكونُ بعدَ تَحقُّقِ حَقيقتِهِ فَلَا يكون ذاتيًّا لِمَا تَحتَهُ مِنَ الأفراد، وإنْ جازَ أنْ يكونَ ذاتيًا لما فيها مِنَ الحِصص ؛ كالماشي لحقيقتِهِ العارضة للحيوانات ا.هـ. وفي الدَّوَّاني : النُّقطة نوع حقيقي، وليست نوعاً إضافيًا، أمَّا الأَوَّلُ ؛ فَلِاتّفاقِ أفرادِهَا ،بالحقيقة، وأمَّا الثَّاني؛ فَلِأنَّها لا تدخل تحتَ مَقولةٍ مِنَ المقولات، وإِنْ دَخلَتْ تحت العرض؛ لكن العرض ليسَ جِنساً لِمَا تحتَهُ، أو لأنَّها بسيطةٌ ؛ أي : فَلَا تكونُ مُركَّبَةً مِنَ الجنس والفصل، فَلا تكونُ نَوعاً إضافيًا ؛ لوجوبِ اندراج النَّوع الإضافي تحتَ الجنس، وكلا الوجهين ضعيفٌ، أَمَّا الأَوَّلُ ؛ فَلِأَنَّهُ لا يدلُّ عَلى أنَّ لا جنسَ لَهَا ، بل على أن لا جنسَ لَهَا عالياً، وربَّما كانَ لَهَا جنس مفرد؛ إذ المنحصر في المقولات هو الأجناسُ العالية فقط، فجازَ أن تكونَ مُركَّبةٌ مِنَ الأجزاء العقلية المتحدة في الوجودِ الخارجي؛ كسائر الماهياتِ المركَّبةِ مِنَ الأجناس والفصول، وأمَّا الثَّاني؛ فَلانَّ البساطة العقلية ممنوعة، والخارجيَّة لا تُجدي نفعاً ؛ لأنَّ الجنس ليس جزءاً خارجيًا ؛ بل هوَ مِنَ الأجزاء العقلية، فجازَ أَنْ يكونَ للنّقطة جزء عقلي، وهو جنس لها ؛ وإن لم يكن لها جنس في الخارج، ثمَّ جعل النسبة هي العموم والخصوص الوجهي ؛ بناءً على ما عليه المتأخرون، وأما
For it is true of it both the true species and the relative species, as appears with minimal reflection. (And their difference) in the genitive, coordinated with his statement 'their agreement'; i.e., for the difference of the two species (in animal and the point). For animal is a relative species, not a true one, and the point is the opposite; because if it were relative, it would be subsumed under a genus, so it would not be simple; this is a contradiction. al-Dasuqi: His statement 'For it is true of it the true species' i.e., with regard to its individuals like Zayd and the like, and the relative [species] with regard to animal. His statement 'the point is the opposite' i.e., it is a true species, not relative; because it is true of individuals that agree in essence, like the end of this line and the end of that line, and it is not subsumed under a genus which is the defining mark of the true [species]. And know that unity is true of the point, but not every unity is a point, and the point, even if it falls under accident, accident is not a genus for what is under it; because accident's predictability of what is under it is by ambiguity (tashkik) and the genus must be predicated of what is under it by univocity (tawatu'). al-Attar: His statement 'the point' and similar are intellect and unity. The validity of the example depends on its individuals agreeing in essence and not falling under any of the ten categories. So it is said regarding the individuals under the concept of the point—which are the point that is the end of a line, the point that is the end of the surface of a cone, the point that occurs in the middle of a line, and the center point—that they are individual instances. If they were made types subsumed under a genus, the example would not be valid. Likewise for the individuals of the ten intellects, and unity under which are personal unity, specific unity, generic unity, accidental unity, connective unity, social unity, and conventional unity. His statement 'Because if it were relative, it would be subsumed under a genus' and the consequent is false, and the implication is apparent. As for the demonstration of the falsity of the consequent, his statement 'then it would not be simple' is an indication. It is said: (1) (His statement: 'And know... etc.') i.e., between them is absolute generality and specificity; unity is distinct from it by unity of the person like Zayd, and unity of the species like man, and unity of the genus like animal, and the point is not distinct from unity; both are true species only. End quote from al-Sharnubi. Chapter on the Principles of Conceptions. It would not be simple; this is a contradiction. al-Dasuqi: His statement 'this is a contradiction' i.e., its being non-simple is a contradiction, i.e., rejected as false, because of its being simple. And in it: if he means 'simple' externally, it is granted but does not harm us; if he means intellectually, then no, because it is the limit of a line, so it is composite, restricted by being the limit of a line; i.e., it is composed of absolute limit and this restriction. Reflect. al-Attar: It is a folded syllogism whose reconstruction: if it were subsumed under a genus, it would not be simple; and the consequent is false because it is contrary to the assumed. It cannot be said: 'It is subsumed under accident' because we say: it is not a highest genus for what is under it from the categories; because it is not essential to them. He said in Sharh al-Maqasid: The meaning of substance is the essence of a thing and its reality, so it is essential. Unlike accident, for its meaning is what occurs to a subject, and the occurrence of something to something is only after the realization of its reality, so it is not essential for the individuals under it, though it may be essential for the parts in it, like 'walking' for the reality that occurs to animals. End quote. And in al-Dawwani: The point is a true species, not a relative species. As for the first, because its individuals agree in reality; and as for the second, because it does not fall under any category, and even if it falls under accident, accident is not a genus for what is under it, or because it is simple; i.e., it is not composed of genus and differentia, so it is not a relative species due to the necessity of a relative species being subsumed under a genus. Both arguments are weak. As for the first, because it does not show that it has no genus, but only that it has no highest genus, and perhaps it has a simple genus; for what is limited to the categories are only the highest genera, so it is possible that it is composed of intellectual parts united in external existence, like other composite quiddities composed of genera and differentiae. As for the second, because intellectual simplicity is denied, and external simplicity is of no use, because the genus is not an external part, but rather one of the intellectual parts; so it is possible that the point has an intellectual part which is its genus, even if it does not have a genus externally. Then he made the relationship that of common and specific in a certain respect (al-umum wa al-khusus al-wajhi), based on what the later scholars hold. And as for
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the distinction between true (haqiqi) and relative (idafi) species, using the examples of animal (hayawan) and the point (nuqta). The commentators explain why the point is a true species and not a relative one. The argument proceeds as follows: First, it is stated that animal is a relative species because it is predicated of individuals (e.g., Zayd) with respect to a higher genus, but not a true species in itself (rather it is a genus for humans). The point, however, is the opposite: it is a true species because its individuals (e.g., endpoints of different lines) agree in essence and it is not subsumed under any genus. The commentator al-Dasuqi clarifies that 'true species' applies to the point when considering its individuals, while 'relative species' applies when considering the point's relation to something else (like a line). Al-Attar adds that the point's individuals are personal instances (afrad shakhsiyya) that share the same reality, so if they were made into types under a genus, the example would fail. The passage then addresses a reductio argument: if the point were a relative species, it would be subsumed under a genus, but then it would not be simple (basiita), contradicting its assumed simplicity. This reductio is elaborated: the point is simple in the sense of not being composed of genus and differentia (though intellectually it may be composite). The discussion then shifts to the nature of accident: accident is not a genus because it is predicated by ambiguity (tashkik) rather than univocally (tawatu'). Later, al-Dawwani's view is cited: the point is a true species because its individuals agree in reality and it does not fall under a category. However, both arguments for the point's simplicity are criticized. The first argument (that it has no genus because it falls under no category) is weak because it only shows it has no highest genus, not that it lacks a simple genus. The second argument (that it is simple) is weak because intellectual simplicity is denied; the genus is an intellectual part, so the point could still have an intellectual genus. Thus, the passage concludes that the relationship between the point and unity is that of common and specific in a certain respect (al-umum wa al-khusus al-wajhi), which is the position of later scholars. Throughout, the commentary exemplifies the use of examples from the Islamic sciences (e.g., Zayd as a personal individual, animal and man as types) to illustrate logical distinctions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the point (nuqta) considered a true species rather than a relative species according to the commentary?
A) It falls under a genus.
B) Its individuals are diverse in essence.
C) Its individuals agree in essence and it is not under a genus.
D) It is composite.

Key Takeaway
A true species is defined by its individuals agreeing in essence and not being subsumed under a higher genus; the point exemplifies this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether 'animal' is a true or relative species when predicated of 'man'. Write one sentence justifying your answer using the criteria from this lesson.
?
Consider the concept of 'substance' (jawhar). Is it a true species or a relative species? Explain with reference to the criteria of individuals agreeing in essence and subsumption under a genus.

The Five Universals
intermediate
10 min
The Reductio Argument for the Point's Simplicity
Commentary presents a reductio argument proving the point is not a relative species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct and evaluate the conditional (reductio) argument that proves the point is not a relative species because it is simple.

Core Idea
If the point were relative, it would not be simple; but it is simple, so it is not relative.

The passage contains a folded syllogism (qiyas matwi) that argues for the point's nature as a true species via reductio ad absurdum. The key claim is that if the point were a relative species, it would be subsumed under a genus, which would contradict its simplicity. We will unpack this logical structure and test its validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional premise
Find the statement: 'If it were relative, it would be subsumed under a genus' (لو كانت إضافية لاندرجت تحت جنس). This is the first conditional.
This is from the main text.
2
Add the second conditional
The commentary adds: 'If it were subsumed under a genus, it would not be simple' (لو اندرجت تحت جنس لم تكن بسيطة). This forms a chain.
The reductio uses modus tollens: If P then Q; if Q then R; not R; therefore not P.
3
Identify the falsity of the consequent
The conclusion that the point is not simple (non-simple) is false because the point is assumed simple (basiita). This is the contradiction (khulf).
Al-Dasuqi explains that 'simple' here can mean external or intellectual simplicity.
4
Reconstruct the folded syllogism
The commentator al-Attar says it is a folded syllogism: if under genus then not simple; not not simple (i.e., it is simple); therefore not under genus; hence not relative.
This is a chain of conditionals.

فإنَّه يصدُقُ عليه النَّوعُ الحقيقي والإضافي، كما يظهر بأدنى تأمل. (وَتَفَارُقِهما ) بالجرّ عطف على قوله : «تصادقهما»؛ أي: لتفارُقِ النَّوعين (فِي الْحَيَوَانِ وَالنُّقْطَةِ، فإنَّ الحيوان نوعٌ إضافي لا حقيقي، والنُّقطة بالعكس؛ لأنَّها لو كانَتْ إضافيَّةٌ ؛ لاندرجت تحت جنس، فلا تكون بسيطةً، هذا خُلْفٌ .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنَّهُ يَصْدُقُ عَلَيْهِ النَّوْعُ الْحَقِيقِيُّ) أي: بالنَّظرِ لأفراده من زيد ونحوه، والإضافي : بالنظر للحيوان.
(قَوْلُهُ : وَالنُّقْطَةُ بِالْعَكْسِ أي : فهي نوع حقيقي؛ لَا إضافي؛ لأنَّها تصدقُ على أفرادٍ مُتَّفقةِ الحقيقة؛ كآخر هذا الخطّ، وآخر هذا الخط، وليست مندرجةً تحت جنس الذي هو ضابط الحقيقي . واعلَمْ (١) أنَّ التُقطةً يصدقُ عليها الوحدة وليس كلُّ وحدةٍ نُقطة، والنُّقطة وإن دخلَتْ تحتَ العَرَضَ ؛ لكنَّ العَرَضَ ليسَ جنساً لِمَا تحته ؛ لأنَّ العَرَضَ ؛ مَقوليتُهُ على ما تحته بالتّشكيكِ والجنس يجب أن تكونَ مَقوليّتُهُ على ما تحتَهُ بالتَّواطؤ .
العطار
هي
(قَوْلُهُ : وَالنُّقْطَةِ) ومثلها العقل والوحدة، وصحَّةُ التَّمثيل بِها ؛ يتوقَّفُ على أنَّ أفرادها مُتفقةُ الحقيقة، وعدم دخولها تحتَ مَقولةٍ مِنَ المقولات العشرِ ؛ فَيُقالُ في الأفرادِ الَّتي تحتَ مَفهوم النُّقطة، وهِيَ النُّقطةُ الَّتِي هِيَ طرفُ الخطِّ ، والنُّقطة التي هِيَ طرفُ سطح المخروط، والنُّقطة التي تعرضُ وسط الخط، ونقطة المركز؛ أنَّها أفرادٌ شَخصيَّةٌ، فلو مُجعِلَتْ أنواعاً مُندرجةً تحتَ جنس ؛ لم يصحَ التَّمثيل، ومثلُهُ في أفراد العقول العشرة، والوحدة تحتها الوحدةُ الشَّخصيَّةُ والنَّوعيَّةُ والجنسيّة والعَرَضيَّةُ والاتصالية والاجتماعية والاعتبارية. (قَوْلُهُ: لِأَنَّهَا لَوْ كَانَتْ إِضَافِيَّةٌ، لَانْدَرَجَتْ تَحْتَ جِنْسِ والتّالي باطل، والملازمة ظاهرةٌ، وأمَّا بيان بطلانِ التَّالي ؛ فَقَولُهُ: فَلَا تكون بسيطةٌ ؛ فَإِنَّهُ إِشارةٌ
يُقالُ
(۱) (قَوْلُهُ : واعلم ... إلخ) أي: فبينهما العموم والخصوص المطلق، تنفرد الوحدة عنها وحدة الشخص كزيد، ووحدة النوع كإنسان ووحدة الجنس ،كحيوان، ولا تنفرد النقطة عن الوحدة، وكلاهما نوع حقيقي لا غير . ا . هـ. الشَّرنوبي.
فصل: في مبادئ التصورات
تكون بسيطةً، هذا خُلْفٌ .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : هَذَا خُلْفٌ) أي : كونها غير بسيطةٍ ؛ خُلْف؛ أي : مطروح وراء الخلف؛ لكونها بسيطة . وفيه : أَنَّهُ إنْ أرادَ بسيطةٌ خارجاً ؛ فمُسلَّم، ولكن لا يضرنَا، وإنْ أراد عقلاً ؛ فَلَا ؛ لأنَّها نهاية الخط، فهي مُركَّبةٌ مُقيَّدةٌ بكونها نهاية الخطّ ؛ أي : إِنَّهَا مُركَّبَةٌ مِن مُطلقِ النّهايةِ، وَمِنْ هذا القيد، تأمل.

It cannot be said: 'It is subsumed under accident' because we say: it is not a highest genus for what is under it from the categories; because it is not essential to them. He said in Sharh al-Maqasid: The meaning of substance is the essence of a thing and its reality, so it is essential. Unlike accident, for its meaning is what occurs to a subject, and the occurrence of something to something is only after the realization of its reality, so it is not essential for the individuals under it, though it may be essential for the parts in it, like 'walking' for the reality that occurs to animals. End quote. And in al-Dawwani: The point is a true species, not a relative species. As for the first, because its individuals agree in reality; and as for the second, because it does not fall under any category, and even if it falls under accident, accident is not a genus for what is under it, or because it is simple; i.e., it is not composed of genus and differentia, so it is not a relative species due to the necessity of a relative species being subsumed under a genus. Both arguments are weak. As for the first, because it does not show that it has no genus, but only that it has no highest genus, and perhaps it has a simple genus; for what is limited to the categories are only the highest genera, so it is possible that it is composed of intellectual parts united in external existence, like other composite quiddities composed of genera and differentiae. As for the second, because intellectual simplicity is denied, and external simplicity is of no use, because the genus is not an external part, but rather one of the intellectual parts; so it is possible that the point has an intellectual part which is its genus, even if it does not have a genus externally. Then he made the relationship that of common and specific in a certain respect (al-umum wa al-khusus al-wajhi), based on what the later scholars hold. And as for
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the distinction between true (haqiqi) and relative (idafi) species, using the examples of animal (hayawan) and the point (nuqta). The commentators explain why the point is a true species and not a relative one. The argument proceeds as follows: First, it is stated that animal is a relative species because it is predicated of individuals (e.g., Zayd) with respect to a higher genus, but not a true species in itself (rather it is a genus for humans). The point, however, is the opposite: it is a true species because its individuals (e.g., endpoints of different lines) agree in essence and it is not subsumed under any genus. The commentator al-Dasuqi clarifies that 'true species' applies to the point when considering its individuals, while 'relative species' applies when considering the point's relation to something else (like a line). Al-Attar adds that the point's individuals are personal instances (afrad shakhsiyya) that share the same reality, so if they were made into types under a genus, the example would fail. The passage then addresses a reductio argument: if the point were a relative species, it would be subsumed under a genus, but then it would not be simple (basiita), contradicting its assumed simplicity. This reductio is elaborated: the point is simple in the sense of not being composed of genus and differentia (though intellectually it may be composite). The discussion then shifts to the nature of accident: accident is not a genus because it is predicated by ambiguity (tashkik) rather than univocally (tawatu'). Later, al-Dawwani's view is cited: the point is a true species because its individuals agree in reality and it does not fall under a category. However, both arguments for the point's simplicity are criticized. The first argument (that it has no genus because it falls under no category) is weak because it only shows it has no highest genus, not that it lacks a simple genus. The second argument (that it is simple) is weak because intellectual simplicity is denied; the genus is an intellectual part, so the point could still have an intellectual genus. Thus, the passage concludes that the relationship between the point and unity is that of common and specific in a certain respect (al-umum wa al-khusus al-wajhi), which is the position of later scholars. Throughout, the commentary exemplifies the use of examples from the Islamic sciences (e.g., Zayd as a personal individual, animal and man as types) to illustrate logical distinctions.

Why Accident Cannot Be a Genus: Tashkik vs Tawatu'
Commentary argues accident cannot be a genus due to ambiguous predication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why accident ('arad) is not a genus for the point or any other entity, using the distinction between ambiguous (tashkik) and univocal (tawatu') predication.

Core Idea
Genus requires univocal predication, but accident is predicated by ambiguity.

One might object that the point falls under accident (al-'arad), so accident could be its genus. The commentators refute this by noting that a genus must be predicated of its species univocally (tawatu'), meaning the same definition applies to all. Accident, however, is predicated by ambiguity (tashkik), as its meaning varies across instances. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its implications for the five universals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim that the point is under accident
The passage states: 'the point, even if it falls under accident, accident is not a genus for what is under it.' Find this statement.
This is in the main text and commentary.
2
Understand tawatu' (univocity)
A genus is predicated of its species with the same meaning applied equally. For example, 'animal' is said of 'man' and 'horse' with the same definition.
Tawatu' is also called 'bi al-tawatu' or 'bil-tawatu'.
3
Understand tashkik (ambiguity)
Accident is predicated of its instances with different meanings (priority and posteriority). For instance, 'white' is said of snow and paper but differently.
Tashkik is also called 'bi al-tashkik'.
4
Apply to the point
The point is an accident, but 'accident' as a universal is not a genus for different accidents because they do not share an essence in the same way.
The commentary quotes Sharh al-Maqasid to show accident is not essential.

لقياس مطوي تقريره : لو اندرجت تحت جنس لم تكن بسيطة، والتّالي باطل؛ لأنَّهُ خلافُ المفروض، لا يُقالُ : مُندرجةٌ تحتَ العَرَضِ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : ليس هو جنساً عالياً لِمَا تحتَهُ مِنَ المقولات؛ لأنَّه ليس ذاتيا لها، قال في شرح المقاصد: المعنى مِنَ الجوهر؛ ذاتُ الشَّيء وحقيقته، فيكون ذاتيًا بِخِلافِ العَرض فإنَّ معناه ما يعرضُ للموضوع، وعروضُ الشَّيءِ لِلشَّيء إِنَّما يكونُ بعدَ تَحقُّقِ حَقيقتِهِ فَلَا يكون ذاتيًّا لِمَا تَحتَهُ مِنَ الأفراد، وإنْ جازَ أنْ يكونَ ذاتيًا لما فيها مِنَ الحِصص ؛ كالماشي لحقيقتِهِ العارضة للحيوانات ا.هـ. وفي الدَّوَّاني : النُّقطة نوع حقيقي، وليست نوعاً إضافيًا، أمَّا الأَوَّلُ ؛ فَلِاتّفاقِ أفرادِهَا ،بالحقيقة، وأمَّا الثَّاني؛ فَلِأنَّها لا تدخل تحتَ مَقولةٍ مِنَ المقولات، وإِنْ دَخلَتْ تحت العرض؛ لكن العرض ليسَ جِنساً لِمَا تحتَهُ، أو لأنَّها بسيطةٌ ؛ أي : فَلَا تكونُ مُركَّبَةً مِنَ الجنس والفصل، فَلا تكونُ نَوعاً إضافيًا ؛ لوجوبِ اندراج النَّوع الإضافي تحتَ الجنس، وكلا الوجهين ضعيفٌ، أَمَّا الأَوَّلُ ؛ فَلِأَنَّهُ لا يدلُّ عَلى أنَّ لا جنسَ لَهَا ، بل على أن لا جنسَ لَهَا عالياً، وربَّما كانَ لَهَا جنس مفرد؛ إذ المنحصر في المقولات هو الأجناسُ العالية فقط، فجازَ أن تكونَ مُركَّبةٌ مِنَ الأجزاء العقلية المتحدة في الوجودِ الخارجي؛ كسائر الماهياتِ المركَّبةِ مِنَ الأجناس والفصول، وأمَّا الثَّاني؛ فَلانَّ البساطة العقلية ممنوعة، والخارجيَّة لا تُجدي نفعاً ؛ لأنَّ الجنس ليس جزءاً خارجيًا ؛ بل هوَ مِنَ الأجزاء العقلية، فجازَ أَنْ يكونَ للنّقطة جزء عقلي، وهو جنس لها ؛ وإن لم يكن لها جنس في الخارج، ثمَّ جعل النسبة هي العموم والخصوص الوجهي ؛ بناءً على ما عليه المتأخرون، وأما
For it is true of it both the true species and the relative species, as appears with minimal reflection. (And their difference) in the genitive, coordinated with his statement 'their agreement'; i.e., for the difference of the two species (in animal and the point). For animal is a relative species, not a true one, and the point is the opposite; because if it were relative, it would be subsumed under a genus, so it would not be simple; this is a contradiction. al-Dasuqi: His statement 'For it is true of it the true species' i.e., with regard to its individuals like Zayd and the like, and the relative [species] with regard to animal. His statement 'the point is the opposite' i.e., it is a true species, not relative; because it is true of individuals that agree in essence, like the end of this line and the end of that line, and it is not subsumed under a genus which is the defining mark of the true [species]. And know that unity is true of the point, but not every unity is a point, and the point, even if it falls under accident, accident is not a genus for what is under it; because accident's predictability of what is under it is by ambiguity (tashkik) and the genus must be predicated of what is under it by univocity (tawatu'). al-Attar: His statement 'the point' and similar are intellect and unity. The validity of the example depends on its individuals agreeing in essence and not falling under any of the ten categories. So it is said regarding the individuals under the concept of the point—which are the point that is the end of a line, the point that is the end of the surface of a cone, the point that occurs in the middle of a line, and the center point—that they are individual instances. If they were made types subsumed under a genus, the example would not be valid. Likewise for the individuals of the ten intellects, and unity under which are personal unity, specific unity, generic unity, accidental unity, connective unity, social unity, and conventional unity. His statement 'Because if it were relative, it would be subsumed under a genus' and the consequent is false, and the implication is apparent. As for the demonstration of the falsity of the consequent, his statement 'then it would not be simple' is an indication. It is said: (1) (His statement: 'And know... etc.') i.e., between them is absolute generality and specificity; unity is distinct from it by unity of the person like Zayd, and unity of the species like man, and unity of the genus like animal, and the point is not distinct from unity; both are true species only. End quote from al-Sharnubi. Chapter on the Principles of Conceptions. It would not be simple; this is a contradiction. al-Dasuqi: His statement 'this is a contradiction' i.e., its being non-simple is a contradiction, i.e., rejected as false, because of its being simple. And in it: if he means 'simple' externally, it is granted but does not harm us; if he means intellectually, then no, because it is the limit of a line, so it is composite, restricted by being the limit of a line; i.e., it is composed of absolute limit and this restriction. Reflect. al-Attar: It is a folded syllogism whose reconstruction: if it were subsumed under a genus, it would not be simple; and the consequent is false because it is contrary to the assumed. It cannot be said: 'It is subsumed under accident' because we say: it is not a highest genus for what is under it from the categories; because it is not essential to them. He said in Sharh al-Maqasid: The meaning of substance is the essence of a thing and its reality, so it is essential. Unlike accident, for its meaning is what occurs to a subject, and the occurrence of something to something is only after the realization of its reality, so it is not essential for the individuals under it, though it may be essential for the parts in it, like 'walking' for the reality that occurs to animals. End quote. And in al-Dawwani: The point is a true species, not a relative species. As for the first, because its individuals agree in reality; and as for the second, because it does not fall under any category, and even if it falls under accident, accident is not a genus for what is under it, or because it is simple; i.e., it is not composed of genus and differentia, so it is not a relative species due to the necessity of a relative species being subsumed under a genus. Both arguments are weak. As for the first, because it does not show that it has no genus, but only that it has no highest genus, and perhaps it has a simple genus; for what is limited to the categories are only the highest genera, so it is possible that it is composed of intellectual parts united in external existence, like other composite quiddities composed of genera and differentiae. As for the second, because intellectual simplicity is denied, and external simplicity is of no use, because the genus is not an external part, but rather one of the intellectual parts; so it is possible that the point has an intellectual part which is its genus, even if it does not have a genus externally. Then he made the relationship that of common and specific in a certain respect (al-umum wa al-khusus al-wajhi), based on what the later scholars hold. And as for

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the distinction between true (haqiqi) and relative (idafi) species, using the examples of animal (hayawan) and the point (nuqta). The commentators explain why the point is a true species and not a relative one. The argument proceeds as follows: First, it is stated that animal is a relative species because it is predicated of individuals (e.g., Zayd) with respect to a higher genus, but not a true species in itself (rather it is a genus for humans). The point, however, is the opposite: it is a true species because its individuals (e.g., endpoints of different lines) agree in essence and it is not subsumed under any genus. The commentator al-Dasuqi clarifies that 'true species' applies to the point when considering its individuals, while 'relative species' applies when considering the point's relation to something else (like a line). Al-Attar adds that the point's individuals are personal instances (afrad shakhsiyya) that share the same reality, so if they were made into types under a genus, the example would fail. The passage then addresses a reductio argument: if the point were a relative species, it would be subsumed under a genus, but then it would not be simple (basiita), contradicting its assumed simplicity. This reductio is elaborated: the point is simple in the sense of not being composed of genus and differentia (though intellectually it may be composite). The discussion then shifts to the nature of accident: accident is not a genus because it is predicated by ambiguity (tashkik) rather than univocally (tawatu'). Later, al-Dawwani's view is cited: the point is a true species because its individuals agree in reality and it does not fall under a category. However, both arguments for the point's simplicity are criticized. The first argument (that it has no genus because it falls under no category) is weak because it only shows it has no highest genus, not that it lacks a simple genus. The second argument (that it is simple) is weak because intellectual simplicity is denied; the genus is an intellectual part, so the point could still have an intellectual genus. The Ascending Arrangement of Genera
Author states that genera may be arranged hierarchically, but the particle 'qad' hints at exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to interpret the role of the particle 'qad' in logical texts and explain the hierarchical arrangement of genera as both actual but not necessary.

Core Idea
The particle 'qad' signals that ordering of genera is actual but not necessary.

In the study of the five universals, we often think of genera forming a neat ladder from species to the highest genus. But the matn states that genera 'may be arranged ascendingly' using the particle 'qad'. This particle is not accidental; it hints that the hierarchy is real but not universal. The commentaries of al-Dasuqi and al-Attar unpack this nuance, teaching us to look for exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Locate the matn's claim about genera arrangement.
Find the statement 'thumma al-ajnāsu qad tatarattabu mutaṣā'idatan' in the Arabic. Note the use of 'qad' before the verb. This is the core claim: genera may be arranged ascendingly.
The word 'thumma' indicates this follows earlier discussion.
2
Analyze the function of 'qad' according to al-Dasuqi.
Al-Dasuqi explains that 'qad' here is for tahqīq (actuality/certainty) not taqlīl (paucity). He says it is used because some genera have no ordering. So 'qad' warns that the arrangement is not universal.
This refutes a common misunderstanding that 'qad' always implies rarity.
3
Understand al-Attar's expansion on necessity.
Al-Attar adds that 'qad' indicates ordering is not obligatory (wājib). Just as there can be a species outside the chain (relative species), so too can there be a genus outside it.
This connects genera to species, showing symmetry.
4
Summarize the teaching on hierarchy.
Conclude: genera can be arranged in a chain from lower to higher, but this is not a necessary feature. The 'qad' points to exceptions—the isolated genera.
This prepares for the next lesson on isolated genus.

فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات (ثُمَّ الأَجْنَاسُ) قد (تَتَرَتَّبُ مُتَصَاعِدَةٌ) بأن يكون جنس فوقه جنس، وهكذا (إِلَى) الجنس (العَالِي). الدسوقي: (قَوْلُهُ : قَدْ تَتَرَتَّبُ) «قد» للتحقيقِ لَا التَّقليل، وأتى بـ «قد»; لأنَّ بعض الأجناس لا ترتيب فيه، وهو الجنس المفرد; أي: الذي ليس فوقه جنس، وليس تحته جنس، بل تحته أنواع كالعقل المطلق، فإنَّهُ جنس مفرد ، بناءً على أنَّ الجوهر ليس جنساً له والعقولُ العَشَرةُ الَّتي تحتَهُ; أنواعٌ مُختلفةٌ بالفصول العطار: (قَوْلُهُ: ثُمَّ الأَجْنَاسُ قَدْ تَتَرَتَّبُ أَشارَ بِلفظ قدْ» إلى أنَّ الترتيب في الأجناس مِمَّا لا يجب; كَمَا لا يجب في الأنواع أيضاً ، فَكَما يكونُ نَوعٌ إِضافِيٌّ لَا نوعَ فَوقَهُ وَلَا تَحتَهُ ; فيكونُ مُفرداً غيرَ واقع في سِلْسِلَةِ التّرتيب; كَذَلِكَ يكونُ جنسٌ لَا جِنْسَ فوقَهُ وَلَا تَحتَهُ; فَيكون مفرداً غير واقع في سِلْسِلَةِ التَّرتيبِ، ويُمَثِّلُونَ لِكُلِّ مِنهُمَا الْحُكَماءُ
Section: On the Principles of Concepts. (Then the genera) may (be arranged ascendingly) such that there is a genus above a genus, and so on (to) the (highest) genus. al-Dasuqi: (His statement: 'qad tatarattabu') 'qad' is for actuality (tahqīq) not for paucity, and he used 'qad' because some genera have no ordering in it, which is the isolated genus; i.e., that which has no genus above it and no genus below it, but rather below it are species—like the absolute intellect, for it is an isolated genus, based on the view that substance is not a genus for it, and the ten intellects under it are species differing by differentiae. al-Attar: (His statement: 'thumma al-ajnāsu qad tatarattabu') He indicated by the word 'qad' that ordering in genera is not necessary, just as it is not necessary in species either. Just as there can be a relative species that has no species above it and no species below it, being isolated and not occurring in a chain of ordering, similarly there can be a genus that has no genus above it and no genus below it, being isolated and not occurring in a chain of ordering. The philosophers give examples for each of them.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory section titled 'On the Principles of Concepts' (Mabādi' al-Taṣawwurāt). The matn (base text) states that genera may be arranged in an ascending hierarchy, where one genus is above another, continuing up to the highest genus. The commentator al-Dasuqi explains that the word 'qad' here indicates actuality (tahqīq) or certainty, not paucity. The reason it is included is that some genera have no ordering—these are called isolated genera (al-jins al-mufrad). An isolated genus is one that has no genus above it and no genus below it; it only has species beneath it. An example is the absolute intellect ('aql muṭlaq), which, according to one position, has no higher genus (substance is not its genus) and its species (the ten intellects) differ by their differentiae. Al-Attar adds that 'qad' points to the fact that ordering is not obligatory. Just as there can be a relative species (naw' iḍāfī) that stands alone outside a chain, so too can there be an isolated genus. The philosophers (ḥukamā') give examples for each. Thus, the passage clarifies that while genera can be arranged hierarchically, this is not a universal necessity.

مبادئ التصورات
قد
ترتيب متصاعد
جنس مفرد
العقل المطلق

Checkpoint

A) That the ordering is rare.
B) That the ordering is actual or certain, but not necessary.
C) That the ordering is impossible.
D) That the ordering applies to all genera without exception.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'qad' in the matn is a deliberate qualifier indicating that the hierarchical arrangement of genera is actual but not necessary, allowing for exceptions like isolated genera.
