Division of Differentia into Near and Remote
Author defines differentia and divides it into near and remote.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given differentia as qareeb or ba'eed based on whether it distinguishes the species from partners in the near or remote genus.

Core Idea
Every differentia is either near or remote; this is a rational, not inductive, division.

This passage explains how the differentia (fasl) is divided into two types: near (qareeb) and remote (ba'eed). This classification depends on which level of genus the differentia distinguishes the species from. The commentator also clarifies why the author of the matn chose a more specific definition of differentia from Ibn Sina's two interpretations, and why the division is exhaustive by reason rather than by empirical enumeration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the differentia's role
Recall that the differentia is a universal predicate that answers 'which thing is it?' in the essence. It distinguishes a species from other species under the same genus. Here, the passage specifies that it distinguishes from 'partners' (musharik) in the genus.
The differentia does not answer 'what is it?' (that is the genus), but 'which thing is it?' within that genus.
2
Understand the basis for division
The differentia must distinguish from partners either in the near genus (jins qarib) or in the remote genus (jins ba'eed). There is no third option; thus the division is exhaustive. This is an intellectual (rational) restriction, not an inductive one.
The author emphasizes this to show that the division is necessary, not merely observed in some cases.
3
Apply the classification to an example
Take the definition of 'human' as 'rational animal'. The genus is 'animal' (near genus). The differentia 'rational' distinguishes humans from other animals. Since it distinguishes from partners in the near genus (animal), it is a near differentia (qareeb). Now consider a differentia that distinguishes humans from partners in a higher genus, e.g., 'substance that is rational and sentient'. Here 'rational and sentient' is a remote differentia because it distinguishes from other substances, not just animals.
Near differentia is more precise and commonly used in complete definitions (hadd haqiqi).
4
Connect to the commentator's choice of definition
The commentator notes that Ibn Sina gave two definitions of differentia: one from al-Isharat (predicated in answer to 'which thing?' in its substance) and one from al-Shifa (predicated on the species in answer to 'which thing?' in its essence from its genus). The author chose the second because it avoids the problem of composition from two coequal components. This choice affects how we understand near and remote differentia.
This shows that even the concept of differentia itself has a genus and differentia, and the author's selection is based on logical consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات 6 وبقوله : «في ذاتِه يخرجُ الخاصَّةُ ; لأنَّها وإن كانَتْ مقولة على الشَّيء في جواب أيُّ شيءٍ هو ؟ , لكن لا في جوهره وذاته، بل في عرضه. ثمَّ الفصلُ إمَّا قريب وإمَّا بعيدٌ ; لأنَّه لا يخلو من أن يميّز النَّوعَ عن مشاركه في الجنس القريب أو عن مشاركه في الجنس البعيد. (فَإِنْ مَيَّزَ) الفصلُ النَّوعَ عَنِ المشَارِكِ)؛ أي: مُشارِكِ النَّوعِ (فِي (قَوْلُهُ : لَكِنْ لَا فِي جَوْهَرِهِ) أي : لكن ليسَ مِن جوهره وذاتياته، وقوله: (بل في عرضِهِ)؛ أي: بل هو من عرضيَّاتِ ذلكَ الشَّيء المقول عليه . قَوْلُهُ : وَذَاتِهِ) عطفُ تفسير . (قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنْ مَيَّزَ الْفَصْلُ المناسب ; أي: الفصلُ بأداةِ التَّفسير ; لأنَّه ربَّما يُتوهّم مِن حذفِهَا أَنَّ المصنف حذف الفاعل في غير محل حذفِهِ، مَعَ أَنَّهُ ضميرٌ وَلَا حذف . العطار (قَوْلُهُ: ثُمَّ الْفَصْلُ إِمَّا قَرِيْبٌ وَإِمَّا بَعِيدٌ قالَ الزَّاهديُّ : فسَّرَ الشَّيخُ الفصل في الإشاراتِ بأنَّهُ الكُلِّيُّ الَّذي يُحمَلُ على الشَّيء في جوابِ : أي شيء هو في جوهَرِهِ؟ وفي الشّفاء بأَنَّهُ الكُلّيُّ المقولُ على النَّوعِ في جوابِ : أَيّ شيءٍ هُوَ في ذاتِهِ مِن جنسِهِ، والأوَّلُ أعمُ مِنَ الثَّاني ; لِصِدْقِهِ على فصلِ مَا لا جنسَ لهُ، وَلَمَّا لم يقم دليل على إمكان تركُبِ الماهيَّةِ مِن أَمرَيْنِ مُتساوييْنِ , بَلْ قامَ الدَّليلُ على امتناعِهِ؛ فَإِنَّ معنى التركيب العقليّ ليس إلا في الماهية التي فيها إبهام وتحصيل اختار المصنِّفُ الثاني، كَمَا يدلّ عليهِ ظاهرُ عِبارتِهِ في تفسير الفصل القريب والبعيد وحصر الفصل فيهما، فإنَّ الظَّاهِرَ مِنَ الحصرِ ; الحصر العقلي دون الاستقرائي. (قَوْلُهُ : فَإِنْ مَيَّزَ الْفَصْلُ النَّوْعَ ليس هذا إشارة إلى أنَّ في كلام المصنفِ حذفُ الفاعِلِ لِكُونِهِ ليسَ مِن مواضعه، ولا أنَّهُ تَفسيرُ لِلضَّمير المستتر في (ميَّزَ) بحذف أداة التَّفسيرِ الَّذي لم يوقف على نص في جوازِهِ أو منعه، بل هو فاعل (مَيَّزَ) مذكورٌ حينئذٍ لما أنَّ كُلَّا مِنَ الشَّرح والمثْنِ مَسوقانِ مَساقَ كلام رجل واحدٍ على نحو صفةٍ التّضمين في البديع، قالَهُ البعض، وهذا كلام أظنُّهُ مِن مخترعاتِهِ، لو سلَّم لهُ؛ انسدَّ
Chapter: On the Principles of Concepts. 6 And by his saying: 'In its essence, the property [specific differentia] is excluded; because even if it is predicated of the thing in answer to 'which thing is it?', it is not in its substance and essence, but rather in its accident.' Then the differentia is either near or remote; because it cannot but distinguish the species from its partner in the near genus or from its partner in the remote genus. (For if) the differentia distinguishes the species from the partner (i.e., partner of the species) in his saying: 'but not in its substance' (i.e., but it is not from its substance and essential attributes), and his saying: 'but in its accident' (i.e., rather it is from the accidental attributes of that thing predicated). His saying: 'and its essence' is an explicative apposition. His saying: 'for if the differentia distinguishes...' is appropriate; i.e., the differentia with the tool of explanation; because it might be imagined from its omission that the author omitted the subject in a place where omission is not allowed, while it is a pronoun and there is no omission. Al-Attar: His saying: 'Then the differentia is either near or remote.' Al-Zahidi said: The Shaykh [Ibn Sina] interpreted the differentia in al-Isharat as 'the universal that is predicated of the thing in answer to 'which thing is it? in its substance', and in al-Shifa as 'the universal predicated of the species in answer to 'which thing is it? in its essence from its genus'. The first is more general than the second, because it applies to the differentia of what has no genus. And since no proof has been established for the possibility of the composition of the quiddity from two coequal things, rather proof has been established for its impossibility—for the meaning of intellectual composition is only in the quiddity that has ambiguity and determination—the author chose the second, as is indicated by the apparent meaning of his expression in the interpretation of the near and remote differentia and the restriction of the differentia to them. For the apparent meaning of the restriction is intellectual restriction, not inductive. His saying: 'for if the differentia distinguishes the species...' This is not an indication that there is omission of the subject in the author's speech because it is not one of its places, nor that it is an interpretation of the implicit pronoun in 'distinguishes' by omitting the tool of explanation for which there is no established text on its permissibility or prohibition. Rather, the subject of 'distinguishes' is mentioned then, because both the commentary and the matn are presented as a single speech in the manner of embedding in badi'. This was said by some. This speech I think is among his inventions; if conceded to him, the matter becomes closed.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and explanatory section on the differentia (fasl). It begins by stating that the property (special differentia) is excluded from the definition of 'what is said in answer to 'which thing?' in essence', because although it answers that question, it does so accidentally, not essentially. Then the differentia is divided into near (qareeb) and remote (ba'eed) based on whether it distinguishes the species from partners in the near genus or in the remote genus. The commentary then discusses the grammatical point that the word 'fasl' in the phrase 'fa-in mayyaza al-fasl' is the explicit subject, not a deleted one, contrary to some interpretations. Al-Attar quotes al-Zahidi comparing two interpretations of differentia by Ibn Sina: one from al-Isharat (universal predicated in answer to 'which thing? in its substance') and one from al-Shifa (universal predicated on the species in answer to 'which thing? in its essence from its genus'). The author of the sharh chooses the second because it avoids the problem of composition of quiddity from two coequal components. The restriction of differentia to only near and remote is said to be intellectual (objective) rather than merely inductive, meaning it is a necessary division. Finally, a grammatical debate is noted about the subject of 'mayyaza' in the matn, with some claiming it is a deleted pronoun explained by 'al-fasl', but the sharh maintains that 'al-fasl' is the explicit subject and both commentary and matn are composed as one utterance.

Checkpoint
What determines whether a differentia is classified as near (qareeb) or remote (ba'eed)?
A) Whether it distinguishes the species from partners in the immediate genus or in a higher genus.
B) Whether it is essential or accidental.
C) Whether it is general or specific in meaning.
D) Whether it is taken from al-Isharat or al-Shifa.

Key Takeaway
Every differentia is necessarily either near (distinguishing from partners in the immediate genus) or remote (distinguishing from partners in a higher genus); this division is rational and exhaustive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether the differentia in the definition of 'wudu' (ritual ablution) is near or remote: 'Wudu is the washing of specific body parts with the intention of worship.' The differentia 'with the intention of worship' distinguishes it from ordinary washing. Which genus does it distinguish from? (Answer: The near genus is 'washing' - it distinguishes from other washings, so it is near differentia.)
?
Construct a definition of 'salat' (prayer) and categorize its differentia as near or remote. Example: 'Salat is a set of prescribed actions and recitations beginning with takbir and ending with taslim, performed with the intention of worship.' The differentia includes 'beginning with takbir and ending with taslim' - this distinguishes it from other acts of worship. It distinguishes within the genus 'acts of worship' (near genus), so it is near differentia.

Differentia: Essence vs. Accident, Proximate vs. Remote
Author defines differentia and divides it into proximate and remote.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the differentia (fasl) from the property (khaassa) and classify a differentia as proximate or remote using the genus level.

Core Idea
The differentia answers 'what is it in its essence' and is either proximate or remote depending on the genus it distinguishes from.

In the five universals, the differentia is what makes a species what it is — its essential distinguishing feature. This lesson unpacks the definition of differentia from the Tadhheeb al-Mantiq, showing how it differs from accidental predicates like property, and how it splits into two types based on the level of genus. Mastering this distinction is key to building sound definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of differentia
Find where the passage defines 'fasl' (differentia). It says it is said in answer to 'what is it' in its essence.
The phrase 'fi dhatihi' (in its essence) is crucial.
2
Contrast differentia with property (khaassa)
The passage explicitly excludes the property because the property answers 'what is it' but accidentally, not essentially. Understand why this exclusion matters.
Property is coextensive but not part of the essence.
3
Identify the two types of differentia
The passage divides differentia into proximate and remote based on which genus it distinguishes the species from: proximate for the immediate genus, remote for a higher genus.
Example: 'rational' distinguishes humans from other animals (proximate genus 'animal').
4
Apply the classification to a new example
Test your understanding: If a differentia distinguishes humans from other living beings (genus 'living'), would it be proximate or remote?
Since 'living' is a higher genus than 'animal', it would be a remote differentia.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات

وبقوله: «في ذاتِه يخرج الخاصَّة؛ لأنها وإن كانت مقولة على الشيء في جواب أيُّ شيء هو؟، لكن لا في جوهره وذاته، بل في عرضه. ثمَّ الفصلُ إمَّا قريب وإمَّا بعيدٌ؛ لأنَّه لا يخلو من أن يميّز النَّوعَ عن مشاركه في الجنس القريب أو عن مشاركه في الجنس البعيد. فإن ميَّزَ الفصلُ النَّوعَ عن المشارك في الجنس القريب فقريب؛ أي: فهو فصل قريب كالنَّاطِقِ المميز للإنسان عن مشاركه في الحيوانية.
Chapter: On the Principles of Concepts. And by his statement: 'in its essence' excludes the property because, although it is said of the thing in answer to 'what is it?', [it is] not in its substance and essence, but rather in its accident. Then the differentia is either proximate or remote, because it cannot but distinguish the species from its partner in the proximate genus or from its partner in the remote genus. If the differentia distinguishes the species from the partner in the proximate genus, then it is proximate; i.e., it is a proximate differentia, like the 'rational' that distinguishes man from his partner in animality.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage defines the differentia (fasl) and clarifies its scope. It opens by distinguishing the differentia from the property (khaassa): both answer 'what is it?', but the property does so accidentally, not essentially. The core definition is then given: the differentia is what is said in answer to 'what is it in its essence?' — it must be part of the substance. Next, the author divides the differentia into two types based on the level of the genus it distinguishes the species from. If it distinguishes from partners in the proximate genus (the closest higher genus), it is called a proximate differentia. If it distinguishes from partners in the remote genus (a higher, less specific genus), it is a remote differentia. The example provided is 'rational' (al-nāṭiq) which distinguishes humans from other animals that share the genus 'animality'. This classification is foundational for understanding how essences are structured in Aristotelian logic as adapted in Islamic thought.

Key Terms
الفصل
الخاصة
الجنس
قريب
بعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes a differentia 'proximate' (qarīb)?
A) It distinguishes the species from all other species.
B) It distinguishes the species from partners in the proximate genus.
C) It is the simplest part of the definition.
D) It is the most general differentia.

Key Takeaway
The differentia must be essential and can be proximate or remote depending on the genus level it distinguishes from.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In the definition of 'sawm' (fasting) as 'abstaining from food, drink, and sexual intercourse from dawn to sunset with intention', identify the differentia and state whether it is proximate or remote relative to the genus 'act of worship'.
?
Distinguish the differentia from the property: Why is 'the property of being a speaker' (an-nāṭiq) not a differentia for humans? (Hint: The passage says the property is accidental, not essential.)

Proximate and Distant Differentia
Author divides differentia into proximate and distant types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a proximate and a distant differentia and correctly classify examples.

Core Idea
The distance of a differentia depends on the genus it distinguishes from.

In logic, a differentia (fasl) is what sets a species apart from others sharing a genus. But how close or far that distinction is depends on which genus we consider. This lesson clarifies the two types with examples from the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the species and its immediate genus (jins qarib)
For example, man has the immediate genus 'animal'. The differentia 'rational' distinguishes man from other animals. This is a proximate differentia because it separates from partners in the closest genus.
Proximate differentia: fasl qarib.
2
Check if the differentia distinguishes from partners in a higher genus
If the differentia distinguishes the species from participants in a more distant genus (like 'growing body' for man), it is a distant differentia. Example: 'sensitive' distinguishes man from plants.
Distant differentia: fasl ba'id.
3
Apply the classification to the given examples
The passage gives 'rational' as proximate and 'sensitive' as distant. Verify: rational distinguishes from animal partners; sensitive from partners in the distant genus 'growing body'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجِنْسِ القَرِيْبِ فَقَرِيبٌ؛ أي: فهو فصل قريب كالنَّاطِقِ المميّز للإنسان عن مشاركه في الحيوانية . (قَوْلُهُ : فَقَرِيبٌ ... إِلَخ) كانَ حقَّهُ أنْ يقول : فَفَصل قريب، وفصل بعيد؛ لأنَّ كلا منهما اسم ... باب الاعتراض على الشَّارحينَ بتغيير كلام المصنِّفَيْنِ، والأحسنُ أَنَّ مِثلَهُ مِن قَبيل حَلِّ المعنى كَمَا في نظائرِهِ، ثمَّ ظاهرُ عبارةِ المصنفِ كما قالَ الجَلالُ أَنَّ مَا لا جنس لَهُ ؛ لَا فصلَ لَهُ ، وإلا ؛ لَكَانَ لَهُ قسمٌ آخَرُ يُميّزُهُ عَنِ المشاركات في الوجودِ لا في الجنس؛ كَمَا في الماهية المركَّبَةِ مِن أمرين متساويين، فإنْ أمكن ؛ كانَ كُلُّ مِنهُمَا فصلاً .ا.هـ. يعني : أنَّ ظاهر عِبارة المصنّف ؛ حيث جعل الفصل المعرَّفَ مُقسَّماً كما هُوَ الظَّاهِرُ ، وأخذ في مفهوم كُلِّ واحدٍ مِنَ القِسمَيْنِ ؛ كَونَهُ مُميَّزاً عَنِ المشاركات في لَهُ ؛ لَّا فصلَ لَهُ، وإلا ؛ لم يكن هذا التقسيم حاصراً، بل كانَ للفصل قِسمْ آخَرُ وَهُوَ مُميّزُ الشَّيْء عَن المشاركات في الوجودِ لَا في الجنس؛ كَمَا لَوْ تُرِكَتْ ماهيَّةٌ موجودةٌ مِنْ أَمرَيْنِ مُتَسَاوِيَيْن على مَا جَوَّزَهُ بعضُهُم، فَإِنَّ كُلَّ واحدٍ منهما فصل لَهَا يميزها عن جميع ما عداهَا مِنَ المشاركات في الوجود، وأشار بِقولِهِ : وظاهرُ إلى جواز كون المقسَّم الفصل المميَّزَ عَنِ المشاركات في الجنسِ دونَ المطلقِ الَّذي هو المعرَّفُ، وذلكَ بأن يكون المرادُ مِنَ الضَّميرِ في يميّز غير المعنى المعرَّف على طريق الاستخدام، قالَ السَّيِّدُ : والصَّوابُ أنْ يُقالَ : الانقسام إلى القريب والبعيدِ لا يتصوَّرُ في الفصول المميَّزةِ عَنِ المشاركات الوجودية، فإنَّ الماهية إذا تركَّبَتْ مِنْ أمورٍ مُتساويةٍ ؛ كانَ تَمييز كُلِّ واحدٍ مِنْهَا لِلمَاهِيَّةِ كَتمييز الآخَرِ بِهَا، فَلَا يُمكنُ عَدُّ بعضِها قريباً وبعضها بعيداً، فَلِذَلِكَ خُصَّ اعتبار الانقسام إلى القريب والبعيد بالفصول المميَّزة عن المشاركات الجنسية ا.هـ. (قَوْلُهُ : أَيْ: فَهُوَ فَصْلٌ قَرِيْبٌ أي : لأَنَّهُ الاسم لا مُجرَّد القريب، ومثلُهُ يُقَالُ في بعيد .
ثم قال: فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات (أَوْ) ميَّزَ النَّوعَ عن مشارِكِهِ في الجنسِ البَعِيدِ؛ فَبَعِيدٌ)، كالحسَّاسِ المميّز للإنسان عن مشاركه في الجنس النامي . والفصل أيضاً إمَّا مُقَوِّمٌ أو مقسم كما قال. و(وَإِذَا نُسِبَ) الفصلُ إِلَى مَا يُمَيِّزُه)؛ (قَوْلُهُ: فِي الْجِنْسِ الْبَعِيْدِ كانَ الأَوْلَى أن يزيدَ : فقط؛ لِئَلَّا يصدق التعريفُ المستفاد من التقسيم على القريب؛ إذ مَا مِنْ فصل قريب إلا وهو يميز عن كلِّ مُشارك في الجنسِ البعيد، فناطق كَمَا مَيَّزَ الإنسان عن الفرس والبغل والحمار المشاركة له في الحيوانية؛ ميَّزَهُ أيضاً عن الشَّجرِ المشاركِ لهُ في الجنس البعيد، وهو: جسم نام . (قَوْلُهُ: وَإِذَا نُسِبَ الْفَصْلُ الأَوْلَى؛ أي: الفصل بأداةِ التَّفسير ؛ لأنَّهُ تفسير لِلضَّميرِ المستترِ النَّائبِ عن الفاعل، فحذفُهَا يوهم أنَّ المصنِّفَ حذف نائب الفاعل. (قَوْلُهُ : إِلَى مَا يُمَيِّزُه) أي : إلى ماهيَّةٍ نوعيَّةٍ يميّزها عن غيرِها مِنَ الماهِيَّاتِ النَّوعيَّة، فناطق وحسَّاسٌ مثلاً ؛ إذا نُسِبَ كلُّ واحدٍ منهما للإنسان؛ كانَ مُقدِّماً له، وَكَذا صاهل ؛ إذا نُسِبَ لِلفرس، وناهق إذا نُسِبَ للحمار ، وقولُنَا : إذا نُسِبَ لِماهيَّةٍ نوعيَّةٍ ؛ يخرج ماهيَّة زيد والصنف، إلا أنْ يُقالَ: إنَّهما داخلانِ في الماهِيَّةِ النَّوعيَّة . (قَوْلُهُ : فِي الْجِنْسِ الْبَعِيدِ أي : فقط، وإلا ؛ يصدقُ التّعريفُ على القريب، إذ مَا مِنْ فصل قريب إلَّا وَهُوَ يُميَّز عن كُلِّ مُشارك في الجنس البعيد. (قَوْلُهُ : وَإِذَا نُسِبَ الْفَصْلُ ... إِلَخ) قال في شرح المطالع : الفصلُ لهُ نِسَبٌ ثلاث؛ نسبةٌ لِلنَّوع ونسبةٌ لِلجنسِ ونسبةٌ إلى حِصَّةِ النَّوعِ مِنَ الجنسِ، أَمَّا نِسبتُهُ إلى النّوعِ ؛ فَبِأَنَّهُ مُقَوِّمٌ لَهُ كَتَقويمِ النَّاطِقِ لِلإنسان، وأمَّا نِسبته إلى الجنسِ ؛ فَبِأَنَّهُ مُقَسّمٌ لَهُ كتقسيم النَّاطِقِ الحيوان إلى الإنسان، وأمَّا نسبتُهُ إلى الحصّةِ؛ فَنَقَلَ الإِمَامُ عَنِ الشَّيخ أَنَّهُ عِلَّةٌ فاعليَّةٌ لوجودِهَا مثلاً مِنَ الحيوان في الإنسانِ حِصَّة، وَكَذَا في الفرس؛ وغيره، والموجدُ للحيوانية التي في الإنسان والناطقيَّةِ وللحيوانية التي في الفرس هو الصَّاهلية ا.هـ.
Of the close genus, it is close; meaning: it is a proximate differentia like 'rational' distinguishing man from his partner in animality. (His saying: 'close' etc.) It should have been said: 'a proximate differentia and a distant differentia' because each of them is a name... Chapter on objecting to the commentators for changing the wording of the authors, and the best is that such is from the category of resolving the meaning as in its parallels. Then the apparent meaning of the author's statement, as al-Jalal said, is that what has no genus has no differentia, otherwise it would have another division distinguishing it from the participants in existence not in genus, as in the quiddity composed of two coextensive things, if possible, each of them would be a differentia. End. Meaning: The apparent meaning of the author's statement, where he made the defined differentia divided as it appears, and took in the concept of each of the two divisions its being distinguishing from the participants in... it has no differentia, otherwise this division would not be exhaustive, but the differentia would have another division which is the distinguisher of the thing from the participants in existence not in genus, as if a existing quiddity is composed of two coextensive things according to what some allowed, then each of them is a differentia for it distinguishing it from all others among the participants in existence. And he indicated by his saying 'and apparent' the permissibility of the divided being the differentia distinguishing from the participants in genus not the absolute which is the defined, and that by intending from the pronoun 'distinguishes' other than the defined meaning in the way of usage. Al-Sayyid said: And the correct is to say: The division into close and distant is not conceivable in differentiae distinguishing from existential participants, for if a quiddity is composed of coextensive things, the distinction of each of them for the quiddity is like the distinction of the other by it, so it is not possible to count some as close and some as distant. Therefore the consideration of division into close and distant is restricted to differentiae distinguishing from generic participants. End. (His saying: 'that is, it is a close differentia' meaning: because it is the name not merely the close, and the like is said in the distant.
Then he said: Section: On the Principles of Conceptualizations. (Or) distinguishes the species from its partner in the distant genus, then it is distant), like 'sensitive' distinguishing man from his partner in the growing genus. And the differentia is also either constitutive or divisive as he said. And (When the differentia is attributed to what it distinguishes); (His saying: 'in the distant genus' it would have been better to add 'only' so that the definition derived from the division does not apply to the close, because there is no proximate differentia except that it distinguishes from every participant in the distant genus. For 'rational' as it distinguishes man from the horse, mule, and donkey participating with him in animality, also distinguishes him from the tree participating with him in the distant genus, which is a growing body. (His saying: 'and when the differentia is attributed' better; meaning: the differentia with a tool of explanation; because it is an explanation of the implicit pronoun standing for the subject, so its omission suggests that the author omitted the subject's deputy. (His saying: 'to what it distinguishes') meaning: to a specific quiddity which it distinguishes from other specific quiddities, so 'rational' and 'sensitive' for example, when each of them is attributed to man, it is a constituent for him, and similarly 'whinnying' when attributed to a horse, and 'braying' when attributed to a donkey. And our saying 'when attributed to a specific quiddity' excludes the quiddity of Zayd and the genus, unless it is said that they are included in the specific quiddity. (His saying: 'in the distant genus' meaning: only, otherwise the definition would apply to the close, because there is no proximate differentia except that it distinguishes from every participant in the distant genus. (His saying: 'and when the differentia is attributed ... etc.') He said in Sharh al-Mutala': The differentia has three relations: a relation to the species, a relation to the genus, and a relation to the share of the species from the genus. As for its relation to the species, it is constitutive of it, like the constitution of 'rational' for man. As for its relation to the genus, it is divisive of it, like the division of 'rational' for animal into man. As for its relation to the share, al-Imam reported from al-Shaykh that it is an efficient cause of its existence, for example from animal in man a share, and likewise in the horse, etc., and the bringer into existence of the animality in man and the rationality and the animality in the horse is the 'whinnying'. End.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the definition and division of the differentia (fasl), one of the five universals. The author begins by explaining that if a differentia distinguishes a species from its partners in the close genus (al-jins al-qarib), it is called a proximate differentia (fasl qarib). The example given is 'rational' (natiq), which distinguishes humans from other animals, all of which share the genus 'animal'. The commentary then addresses a potential criticism: why doesn't the original author say 'a proximate differentia and a distant differentia'? The response is that the expression is from the category of 'resolving the meaning' (hall al-ma'na), not a literal omission. A crucial point follows: the division into proximate and distant only applies to differentiae that distinguish from participants in a genus, not from participants in existence (wujud). For example, if a quiddity is composed of two co-equal components, each could serve as a differentia distinguishing from all existential participants, but they cannot be classified as proximate or distant because the distinction is not relative to a genus. This is confirmed by al-Sayyid's quote that such a division is inconceivable for differentiae distinguishing from existential participants. The passage then transitions to a new section titled 'Principles of Conceptualizations' (mabadi' al-tasawwurat), where the distant differentia is defined: it distinguishes the species from its partner in the distant genus, like 'sensitive' (hassaas) distinguishing humans from plants (the distant genus being 'growing body'). The author adds that a differentia is either constitutive (muqawwim) of the species or divisive (muqassim) of the genus. The final part discusses the relational aspect: when a differentia is attributed to what it distinguishes (i.e., the specific quiddity), it is a constituent; when attributed to the genus, it is divisive; and a third relation to the 'share' (hissa) of the genus in the species, where it is an efficient cause. For example, 'whinnying' (sahil) is the efficient cause of the horse's animality. Throughout, the commentary ensures precision: the definition of distant differentia must be restricted to 'only' (faqat) the distant genus, otherwise the definition would also apply to proximate differentiae, since a proximate differentia like 'rational' also distinguishes from partners in the distant genus (e.g., plants).

فصل بعيد
جنس قريب
جنس بعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a distant differentia (fasl ba'id)?
A) 'Rational' (natiq) for man, because it distinguishes man from animals.
B) 'Sensitive' (hassaas) for man, because it distinguishes man from plants.
C) 'Whinnying' (sahil) for horse, because it distinguishes horse from other animals.
D) 'Growing' (nami) for plant, because it distinguishes plants from inanimate objects.

Key Takeaway
The division into proximate and distant differentia depends on the genus level at which the distinction is made.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the species 'salat' and consider its differentia 'specific actions and recitations'. Identify its proximate genus (e.g., worship) and distant genus (e.g., bodily actions). Then state whether the differentia is proximate or distant, and why.
